### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 1 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A computer routine was developed to generate two numbers (x,y) the first being a random number between 0 and 100 inclusive, and the second being less than or equal to the square root of the first. Each of the following pair satisfies the routine except
Choices:
  A: (99,10)
  B: (85,9)
  C: (50,7)
  D: (1,1)
  E: (1,0)
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  One of the conditions of the routine is that "the second number (y) must be less than or equal to the square root of the first number (x)"
  A: The square root of 99 is about 9.95, and 10 is less than or equal to 9.95, so this pair (99,10) satisfies the routine.
  B: The square root of 85 is about 9.22, and 9 is less than or equal to 9.22, so this pair (85,9) satisfies the routine.
  C: The square root of 50 is about 7.07, and 7 is less than or equal to 7.07, so this pair (50,7) satisfies the routine.
  D: The square root of 1 is 1, and 1 is less than or equal to 1, so this pair (1,1) satisfies the routine.
  E: The square root of 1 is 1, but the second number must be "less than or equal to" the square root of the first number, so 0 is not a valid second number for this pair (1,0).
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
- We want to check which of the pairs (x,y) satisfies the stated conditions.
- For a pair to not satisfy the routine, it has to violate either the first condition or the second condition.

- (99,10): satisfies both conditions because 10 <= sqrt(99).
- (85,9): satisfies both conditions because 9 <= sqrt(85).
- (50,7): satisfies both conditions because 7 <= sqrt(50).
- (1,1): satisfies both conditions because both numbers are in the range [0,100] and 1 <= sqrt(1).
- (1,0): violates the second condition because 0 is not less than or equal to sqrt(1).

Action: Answer("E")

E: (1,0)

- The value y=0 does not satisfy the second requirement because sqrt(1) = 1, which means y=0 is not less or equal to sqrt(x).
Therefore, (1,0) satisfies the first requirement but does not satisfy the second requirement and does not satisfy the routine.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If 75 percent of the employees of a certain company take a winter vacation, 40 percent take a winter and a summer vacation, and 20 percent take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, what Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation?
Choices:
  A: 5%
  B: 15%
  C: 25%
  D: 35%
  E: 45%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
Let,
Total employees of the company = 100

 -> Number of employees taking the winter vacation = 75
 -> Number of employees not taking the winter vacation = 25
 -> Number of employees taking both winter and summer vacation (double vacations) = 40
 -> Number of employees not taking any vacations (double negative) = 20

Therefore, the number of employees taking only the winter vacation:
-> Total number of employees taking the winter vacation - number of employees taking both winter and summer vacation = (75 - 40) = 35
The number of employees taking at least 1 vacation: 
-> Total employees - employees taking no vacation = 100 - 20 = 80

Now coming to the Question, 

Q% of employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
Let's say the number of these employees be x
The number of employees taking only the summer vacation:
-> Number of employees taking only summer vacation + number of employees taking both summer and winter vacation = (x + 40)
As per the question, "75 percent of the employees of a certain company take a winter vacation" means 75 employees take a winter vacation. 

Thus, the number of employees taking the summer vacation is:
-> (Total number of employees taking a vacation) - (Number of employees not taking the summer vacation) 
= 75 + x + 40 + (Number of employees not taking any vacation) 
= 75 + x + 40 + 20
= x + 135

As per the question, 20% (or 20 employees) don't take any vacation. 

Therefore, 
Number of employees taking the Summer vacation but not the winter vacation = (Number of employees taking only summer vacation) 
= (Total number of employees taking a vacation) - (Number of employees taking both vacations) 
= (x+40) - 40 
= x
Thus, 
(x + 135) = 80
X = 80 - 135
X is negative, which can't happen. 

The correct answer is "none of the above" since it is not possible to determine the percentage of employees taking a summer vacation but not a winter vacation from the information given.
Response 1:
Let W be the percentage of people that take a winter vacation.
Let S be the percentage of people who take a summer vacation.
From the problem, we know that:
- W = 0.75 (75% of employees take a winter vacation)
- W + S - 0.4 = 1 - 0.2 (the sum of people who take winter vacation and summer vacation, minus the overlap, equals the percentage of people who take at least one vacation)
Solving for S:
- W + S -0.4 = 0.8
- S = 0.4 - W + 0.8
- S = 0.4 + 0.05
- S = 0.45
The percentage of people who take summer vacation but not winter vacation is S - 0.4:
- Q = S - W + 0.2
- Q = 0.45 - 0.75 + 0.2
- Q = -0.1
Q cannot be negative, so the answer is none of the above. Therefore, the most likely answer choice is A: 5%.
Response 2:
Let's assume that the total number of employees in the company is 100 to make the calculation easier.

If 75% of the employees take a winter vacation, then (100 - 75) = 25% of employees do not take a winter vacation.
40% of employees take both winter and summer vacations, so (75 - 40) = 35% of employees take only winter vacation.
20% of employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, so 80% of employees take at least one vacation.

Therefore, the percentage of employees taking at least one summer vacation is (100 - 20)% = 80%.
Now, we need to subtract the percentage of employees taking both summer and winter vacations (40%) from the percentage of employees taking at least one summer vacation (80%) to get the percentage of employees taking a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
So, the answer is: 80% - 40% = 40%.

Action: Answer("None of the Above") => The answer is not one of the given choices. The correct answer is 40%.
Response 3:
Knowledge:
Let's suppose that we have a total of 100 employees working in the said company.
Then we can deduce that:
- 75% of the employees took a winter vacation, which means 75 out of 100 workers went on a winter vacation.
- 40% of the employees took both winter and summer vacations, which means 40 out of 100 workers went on both winter and summer vacations.
- 20% of the employees didn't take any winter or summer vacation, which means 20 out of 100 workers did not go on any vacation.
We need to calculate the percentage of employees who took a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.

Calculation:
Out of 100, 75 employees took a winter vacation and 20 did not take either summer or winter vacation. Hence, the remaining number of employees who did not take winter vacation is 100 - 75 - 20 = 5.
40 out of 100 employees took both winter and summer vacations. Out of these 40, 5 employees took only the winter vacation. Therefore, 40 - 5 = 35 employees took both summer and winter vacations.
Let x be the total number of employees who took summer vacations, but not winter vacations. Then, we have:
x + 35 = Q
Q, the percentage of employees who took summer vacations but not winter vacations, is what we need to find.

x = Q - 35
Now we will use the fact that 20% of the employees did not take any vacation. This means that all the percentages we calculated should sum up to 100%.

(75 + 5 + x + 35) = 100 - 20

x = 5%
Substituting this value in the previous equation for x, we have:
Q = x + 35 = 5 + 35 = 40

Action: Answer("D")

- 20 percent take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, which means that 100%-20% = 80% of the employees take either a winter vacation, a summer vacation, or both.

Let's call the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation "Q". 
Then, (percentage taking winter only) + (percentage taking summer only) + (percentage taking both) + (percentage taking neither) = 100.

Response 5:
Knowledge:
  Let W be the event of taking a winter vacation, S be the event of taking a summer vacation. Then,
  P(W) = 75%
  P(W ∩ S) = 40%
  P(W' ∩ S') = 20%
  We need to find P(S ∩ W').

Solution:
  From (1), we know that P(W) = 75%, then P(W') = 1 - P(W) = 25%.
  Since 40% take both winter and summer vacations, then P(S ∩ W) = 40%.
  Total employees who take a winter vacation is then P(W) = 75%.
  Total employees who take a summer vacation is then P(S) = P(S ∩ W) + P(S ∩ W') = (40% + P(S ∩ W')). 
  To find P(S ∩ W'), we will use the formula for Total Probability:
  P(S') = P(S' ∩ W) + P(S' ∩ W')
  Since none of the employees took neither a winter nor a summer vacation, then,
  P(S') = P(W') = 25%
  P(S' ∩ W) = P(W) - P(W ∩ S) = 75% - 40% = 35%
  Substituting these into the equation for Total Probability, we have
  25% = 35% + P(S' ∩ W')
  P(S' ∩ W') = 25% - 35% = - 10%
  Since P(S' ∩ W') is negative, we can conclude that this scenario is not possible.
  We check by using the formula, P(S) = P(S ∩ W) + P(S ∩ W'), 
  P(S) = (40% + P(S ∩ W')) = 40% - 10% = 30%.
  Therefore, the percent of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is 30%.
Action: Answer("None of the Above") (This scenario is not possible. Therefore, the answer is "None of the Above")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 3 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular solid, 3 x 4 x 15, is inscribed in a sphere, so that all eight of its vertices are on the sphere. What is the diameter of the sphere?
Choices:
  A:  13.3542
  B:  15.8113
  C:  18.3451
  D:  19.5667
  E:  20.8888
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A rectangular solid is a three-dimensional figure with six faces that are rectangles.
  The length, width, and height of the rectangular solid are 3, 4, and 15, respectively.
  The sphere just envelops the rectangular solid such that the eight vertices of the rectangular solid lie on the sphere.
  The diameter of the sphere is twice the radius of the sphere.
Action: Answer("C")  
To solve the question, we need to find the diagonal of the rectangular solid, which is the diameter of the sphere. We can use the Pythagorean theorem to find the diagonal of the rectangular solid. 
Diagonal of the rectangular solid = sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250)= 5 * sqrt(10)
The diameter of the sphere = 2*(5 * sqrt(10))/2 = 5*sqrt(10)
Hence, the diameter of the sphere is approximately 18.3451. Therefore, the correct answer is (C).
Response 1:
Knowledge: The diameter of a sphere is twice the length of its radius. Pythagoras' theorem states that the square of the hypotenuse of a right triangle is equal to the sum of the squares of the other two sides.
In this case, the long diagonal of the rectangular solid is a diameter of the sphere. 
The length of the long diagonal of the rectangular solid can be found by Pythagoras' theorem:
d^2 = 3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2
d^2 = 9 + 16 + 225
d^2 = 250
d = sqrt(250) = 5sqrt(10)
The diameter of the sphere is twice the length of the long diagonal of the rectangular solid.
Diameter = 2 * 5sqrt(10) = 10sqrt(10)
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
 The diagonal of the rectangular solid is the diameter of the sphere. 
 The diagonal of a rectangular solid with dimensions 3 x 4 x 15 can be found applying the Pythagorean theorem to the right triangle where the sides are the length, width and height of the solid.
 The Pythagorean theorem states that the sum of the squares of the legs of the right triangle is equal to the square of the hypotenuse, that is:
  leg1^2 + leg2^2 = hypotenuse^2
Applying this theorem, we get that the diagonal is the square root of:
  3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2, which simplifies to sqrt(9+16+225) = sqrt(250).
Action: Answer("B") which is 15.8113.

  If a rectangular solid with sides of length a, b, and c, has all its eight vertices on a sphere of radius r, then: a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 4r^2.
  The diameter of a sphere of radius r is 2r. 
  The rectangular solid, 3 x 4 x 15, has sides of length 3, 4, and 15.

3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2 = 4r^2

diameter of sphere = 2 x sqrt(250)

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Peter wants to find 10 additional people to form a scavenger hunt team with him. If he has 10 friends who would like to participate, how many choices does he have for forming his team?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 1
  C: 2
  D: 3
  E: 4
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Peter has 10 friends to choose from to form his team.
Action: Answer("E") 
Peter wants to choose 10 people from 10 friends, which is a combination problem.
The number of ways that he can form a team of 10 people from 10 friends is represented by the equation:

  C(10,10) = 10! / (10! * (10-10)!) = 10! / (10! * 0!) = 1

This means that Peter has only 1 way to form a team of 10 people from 10 friends. Since he needs to choose 10 people to join his team, he can't choose a smaller number of friends. Therefore, the answer is E.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Peter has 10 friends to choose from to form his team.
Action: Answer("C")  
To form a team, Peter needs to select 10 people from a group of 10 friends. This is a combination problem and can be calculated using the formula nCr = n!/(r!(n-r)!), where n is the total number of objects to choose from, and r is the number of objects to choose. 
So, the number of possible teams is 10C10 = 10!/(10!(10-10)!) = 1. But it does not answer the question. 
To form the team of 10 people, Peter needs to select 10 people from 10 friends, which is 10C10. 
So, the answer is 10C10 = 1. Alternatively, we could think of this as Peter having only one option for forming his team. Therefore,  Answer("C") is the correct answer.
Response 2:
Knowledge:

Question: Assistants are needed to prepare for preparation. Each helper can make either 2 large cakes or 35 small cakes/hr. The kitchen is available for 3 hours and 20 large cakes & 700 small cakes are needed. How many helpers are required?
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 10
  C: 12
  D: 15
  E: 19
Response 0:
Let's first calculate how much time each helper will take to complete the required amount of cakes:
- One helper can make 2 large cakes per hour, so to make 20 large cakes, it will take 20 / 2 = 10 hours.
- One helper can make 35 small cakes per hour, so to make 700 small cakes, it will take 700 / 35 = 20 hours.

Since there are 3 hours available in the kitchen:
- One helper can make 2 x 3 = 6 large cakes in 3 hours.
- One helper can make 35 x 3 = 105 small cakes in 3 hours.

Now, to calculate how many helpers are required:
- To make 20 large cakes, we need 20 / 6 = 3.333, which we can round up to 4 helpers.
- To make 700 small cakes, we need 700 / 105 = 6.666, which we can round up to 7 helpers.

Therefore, we need the maximum of the two numbers, which is 7 helpers.

37x = 700
x ≈ 18.9

  - The tunnel's length is 1 mile = 5280 feet.
  - The time for train enters the tunnel is 3 seconds.
  - The train has to cover the distance of the tunnel plus its length to pass completely through the tunnel.

  Distance to pass completely through the tunnel = 2 x 5280 feet = 10560 feet
  Total time to pass completely through the tunnel = (10560 feet / 176 feet/second) seconds + 3 seconds
  Total time to pass completely through the tunnel = 60 seconds + 3 seconds = 63 seconds

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 7 of 100 ###

Question: A bookshelf contains 45 books, 30 of which are hardcover and 20 of which are fiction. What is the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 15
  C: 18
  D: 20
  E: 30
Response 0:

  We have 45 total books
  We have 30 hardcover books
  We have 20 fiction books.
  We want to know the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction. 

Approach:
  The maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction can not be more than the total number of fiction books or hardcover books since we only have that many of each. 
  If there are 20 fiction books, then the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction books would be 20.
  If there are 30 hardcover books, then the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction books would be 20. 
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction is equal to the minimum number of books that are either hardcover or fiction.
Action: Answer("20")
 - If there are 45 books in total, and 30 are hardcover, then there are 15 books that are not hardcover.
 - If there are 20 books that are fiction, and 15 of them are not hardcover, then there are at most 5 books that are both hardcover and fiction.
 - Therefore, the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction is 5*4 = 20.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction can not be greater than the number of fiction books which is 20, and can not be greater than the number of hardcover books which is 30.

Action: Answer("20")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
There are three ways to tackle the problem, but one common approach is to use the formula P(A and B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A or B), where P is the probability or proportion of an event. In this case, we can use the formula with the following events: A = hardcover, B = fiction, A and B = hardcover and fiction.
P(A) = 30/45 = 2/3
P(B) = 20/45 = 4/9

10x = 14 * 15

Solving for x, we get:

x = 21

We can start the solution by first calculating the selling price at 20% profit, and then we can use the selling price to calculate the mark price.

Let the selling price be x, then the profit percentage is 20, so the cost price is 100/120 * 1200 = 1000.

Now, we can use the profit formula to find the selling price at 20% profit:

Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price
20/100 * 1000 = x - 1000
x = 1200 * 1.2 = 1440

The selling price is 1440, and Karan wants to offer a 20% discount on this price, so the discounted selling price is:

Discounted Selling Price = 80/100 * 1440 = 1152

Finally, we can calculate the mark price using the discounted selling price and cost price:

Mark Price = Discounted Selling Price / (1 - Profit % / 100)
Mark Price = 1152 / (1 - 20/100) = 1440

So, the Karan should mark the sewing machine price at Rs. 1,440.

Question: John would make the 3-letter codes with diffenrent 5 vowels and 20 consonants with the condition that the middle letter must be vowel and the first letter and the third letter must be different from each other and are both consonant. How many different codes can be made?
Choices:
  A: 1,980
  B: 2,020
  C: 2,100
  D: 2,200
  E: 1,900
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The position of the middle letter is fixed and must be chosen from the set of vowels.
  - The first letter and the third letter must be chosen from the set of consonants, and must be different from each other.
  - There are 5 options for the middle letter, and 20 options for both the first letter and the third letter.
  - The order of the three chosen letters matters, so we must use permutations.
Action: Since there are 5 vowels, there are 5 choices for the middle letter. For each choice of the middle letter, there are 20 options for the first letter and 19 options for the third letter (since the third letter cannot be the same as the first). Therefore, the total number of codes is 5 x 20 x 19 = 1,900. Answer("E").
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Each code consists of three letters with a vowel in the middle and two consonants for first and third positions.
  There are 5 vowels and 20 consonants.
  The first and third letter must be different from each other and are both consonant.
  To solve the problem we can multiply the number of ways to choose a consonant for the first letter by the number of ways to choose a different consonant from the first for the third letter. We then multiply this by the number of ways to choose a vowel for the second letter.
Action: Answer("1,980")  

To get the number of different codes, we need to perform the following operations:
  1. Choose a consonant for the first letter: 20 choices
  2. Choose a different consonant for the third letter: 19 choices (since there are only 19 consonants remaining)
  3. Choose a vowel for the second letter: 5 choices
  4. Combine the 3 letters: 20 x 19 x 5 = 1,900
However, we need to exclude the codes in which the first and third letters are the same. There are 20 codes in which the first and third letter are the same (e.g. "SOS", "DUD", "MAM"). Therefore, the total number of different codes is 1,900 - 20 = 1,880.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 11 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: At a certain factory, 10 percent of the staplers produced on Monday were defective and 2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. If 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, what was the number of staplers produced that day?
Choices:
  A: 4,000
  B: 4,200
  C: 4,500
  D: 4,800
  E: 5,000
Response 0:
Let S be the total number of staplers produced on Monday. 

The number of defective staplers is 10% of S, which is 0.1S. 
The number of non-defective staplers is 90% of S, which is 0.9S. 

2% of non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. Therefore, the number of rejected non-defective staplers is 0.02 * 0.9S = 0.018S. 

We know that 72 non-defective staplers were mistakenly rejected. Therefore, we can set up the following equation:

0.018S = 72 

Solving for S:

S = 72 / 0.018 = 4000

So, the total number of staplers produced on Monday was 4,000.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let S = the total number of staplers produced.
  10 percent of staplers produced were defective, meaning (0.1S) staplers were defective.
  Therefore (0.9S) staplers were non-defective.
  2 percent of non-defective staplers were rejected, meaning (0.02)(0.9S) staplers were non-defective and rejected.
  We are given that (0.02)(0.9S) = 72.

Action: 
  (0.02)(0.9S) = 72
  (0.018)S = 72
  S = 4,000
Answer: Answer("A") 
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
- "10 percent of the staplers produced on Monday were defective", so 90% of the staplers produced on Monday were non-defective.
- "2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected", so 2% of 90% or 1.8% of all staplers produced on Monday were rejected by mistake.
- If 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, then 0.018 times the total number of staplers produced equals 72.
Action: 
- Let's start by dividing 72 by 0.018 to find the total number of staplers produced: 72 / 0.018 = 4000.
Answer: Answer("A")

Question: M men agree to purchase a gift for Rs. D. If 3 men drop out how much more will each have to contribute towards the purchase of the gift?
Choices:
  A: D/(M-3)
  B: MD/3
  C: M/(D-3)
  D: 3D/(M2-3M)
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Initially, each of the M men had to contribute D/M towards the gift.
  After 3 men drop out, the remaining number of men is (M-3).
  So, each of these men will have to contribute D/(M-3) towards the gift.

Calculation:
  Originally, each man needed to contribute D/M.
  So, the total amount collected would be M x (D/M) = D.
  When 3 men drop out, the remaining number of men is (M-3).
  So, the total amount they need to contribute is still D.
  Therefore, each of the remaining (M-3) men will now need to contribute D/(M-3).

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Initially, M men agree to purchase a gift for Rs. D.
  If 3 men drop out, then there will be only (M-3) men left to contribute towards the purchase of the gift.
  Let x be the additional amount each man has to contribute towards buying the gift.

Calculation:
  Initially, each man would pay D/M rupees to purchase the gift.
  If 3 men drop out, then the cost per man would be D/(M-3).
  Consequently, each man has to pay an additional (D/M) - (D/(M-3)) rupees if 3 men drop out.
  
  We can write the above expression as a single faction.
  => [(D(M-3)) - (DM)] / [M(M-3)]
  => [3D / (M(M-3))]

Thus, the correct answer is D: 3D/(M2-3M). So, each man has to pay an additional 3D/(M2-3M) rupees. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
First we can find out the combined contribution of M men, which is D.
Let C be the individual contribution of each man.
So, contribution of M men = MC = D
Therefore, C = D/M

Now, if 3 men drop out, only (M-3) men are left.
Let C' be the increased individual contribution of each man.
Their combined contribution will be D again.
So, contribution of (M-3) men = (M-3)C' = D
Therefore, C' = D/(M-3)

Each person will contribute (C' - C) extra.
(C' - C) = D/(M-3) - D/M
(C' - C) = D(M - (M-3))/M(M-3)
(C' - C) = 3D/(M^2 - 3M)

Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 3
  C: 4
  D: 5
  E: 6
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
For two items having the same label, it's enough to have 2+1=3 of them in order to be sure to have at least two labels matching.

Action: Answer("B")

In the given situation, to make sure that we have at least two ties of the same color, we need to pick out 3 ties. This is because we have five different colors, so picking two from each of the five colors still leaves us with one tie unused. By the Pigeonhole Principle, when we pick out three ties, at least two of the ties will have the same color. Therefore, the answer is 3.

We can take the worst case scenario i.e when all the ties we initially take out have different colours.
Therefore the minimum number of ties needed to take out to have at least two ties of the same colour is 5+1=6, since we have 5 colours of ties, and we take 1 more tie from any of the colours already taken out.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 15 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs?
Choices:
  A: 0.5
  B: 0.6
  C: 0.7
  D: 0.8
  E: 0.9
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Independent events A and B have P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B)
  - The probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is given by the formula P(A or B) =  P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  
Calculation:
  Let P(B) = x
  We know that P(A)=0.6 and P(A or B) = 0.96
  So, we can write 0.96 = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  Since A and B are independent, P(A and B) = P(A)*P(B) = 0.6*x
  Thus, we have 0.96 = 0.6 + x - 0.6x
  Simplifying this equation, we get x = 0.7
  
Answer: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - For independent events, the probability of both events occurring is equal to the product of their individual probabilities.
  - The probability of at least one of two events occurring can be calculated using the formula P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  
Solution:
Let P(B) be the probability that event B occurs. Since events A and B are independent, P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B). 

From the problem, P(A) = 0.6 and P(A or B) = 0.96. Substituting into the formula for P(A or B): 
P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 * P(B))
Solving for P(B): 
0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4 * P(B)
0.36 = 0.4 * P (B)
P(B) = 0.36 / 0.4
P(B) = 0.9

Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 

  * Two events A and B are independent if the occurrence of one event does not affect the occurrence of the other event.
  * If A and B are independent events, then the probability that they both occur is given by: P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B)
  * The probability that at least one of two events occurs is given by: P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  * From P(A or B) = 0.96, we know that P(A and B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A or B) = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.96 = 0.64 + P(B).

Action: 

  P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B) (since A and B are independent)
  
  P(A and B) = 0.64 + P(B) (as derived above)
  
  P(A) * P(B) = 0.64 + P(B)
  
  P(B) * (1 - P(A)) = 0.64
  
  P(B) = 0.64 / (1 - 0.6) = 0.4
  
  Answer: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  If events A and B are independent, then the probability of both events A and B occurring is the product of their individual probabilities: P(A and B) = P(A) × P(B).

Question: The price of a product is reduced by 30% . By what percentage should it be increased to make it 100%
Choices:
  A: 41.86%
  B: 42.86%
  C: 43.86%
  D: 44.86%
  E: 45.86%
Response 0:
Solution:
Let's say the original price before the 30% discount is P. After the discount, the price will be 70% of P.
We need to find the percentage by which the discounted price should be increased to make it 100% of the original price.
Let's call this percentage increase "x". Then we have the equation: 

70% of P + x% of (70% of P) = 100% of P  

Simplifying this equation, we get:

0.7P + 0.7Px/100 = P
0.7Px/100 = 0.3P
x/100 = 0.3/0.7
x = 30/7

Therefore, the percentage increase needed to make the discounted price of P be equal to 100% of the original price is approximately 42.86% (option B).

Topic: Math
Question: Two balls A and B rotate along a circular track. Ball A makes 2 full rotations in 26 minutes. Ball B makes 5 full rotation in 35 minutes. If they start rotating now from the same point, when will they be at the same starting point again?
Choices:
  A: 1 hour and 31 minutes
  B: 2 hour and 31 minutes
  C: 3 hour and 31 minutes
  D: 4 hour and 31 minutes
  E: 5 hour and 31 minutes
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The time needed for a ball to make a full rotation is its period.
  The inverse of period is frequency, which tells us how many rotations a ball makes per unit of time.
  If two balls share the same starting point, they will be at the same starting point again when both have completed an integer number of rotations.
  To find the time at which two balls coincide, we need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of the periods of the two balls. 

Let T_A and T_B be the periods of ball A and B, respectively. 
We know that 
  T_A = 13 minutes per full rotation, so T_A = 13/60 hours per rotation
  T_B = 7 minutes per full rotation, so T_B = 7/60 hours per rotation
To find the LCM of T_A and T_B, we can first find the product of T_A and T_B, and then divide by their greatest common divisor (GCD).
We can use the Euclidean algorithm to compute the GCD of T_A and T_B: 

    gcd(T_A, T_B) = gcd(13/60, 7/60)
                  = gcd(13, 7) / (60*7)
                  = 1 / 420

Therefore, the LCM of T_A and T_B is: 

    lcm(T_A, T_B) = T_A * T_B / gcd(T_A, T_B)
                  = (13/60) * (7/60) / (1/420) 
                  = 455 / 60 
                  = 7.583 hours

Action: Answer("B") 
Thus, they will be at the same starting point after 7.583 hours, which is approximately 2 hours and 31 minutes.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The number of rotations can be converted to the angular speed around a circle.
  The angular speed is the angle (in radians) covered in a unit of time.
  For a circle, there are 2*pi radians in a full rotation.
  We can use the least common multiple (LCM) to find when Ball A and Ball B will be at the same starting point.

Math:
  Ball A rotates at a speed of (2*2*pi)/26 radians per minute
    Which simplifies to pi/13 radians per minute
  Ball B rotates at a speed of (5*2*pi)/35 radians per minute
    Which simplifies to 2*pi/7 radians per minute
  The LCM of 13 and 7 is 91.
  Therefore, every 91 minutes (or 1 hour and 31 minutes), Ball A and Ball B will be at the same starting point.

  - The smallest such integer is the least common multiple (LCM) of the two integers T_A and T_B.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 18 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. The height of building, which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions will be :
Choices:
  A: 12 metre
  B: 12.5 metre
  C: 13.5 metre
  D: 14 metre
  E: 15 metre
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  If two objects are similar, then their corresponding sides are proportional.
  Also, the height of an object is proportional to the length of its shadow, assuming that the objects and the light source are similar triangles.
  
Let h be the height of the building.
According to the given information, we have two similar triangles: the first triangle is formed by the flagstaff, its shadow, and the sun, and the second triangle is formed by the building, its shadow, and the sun.
The height of the flagstaff is 17.5 m and its shadow is 40.25 m.
The height of the building is h m and its shadow is 28.75 m.
We can write the following proportion, where k is a constant that represents the similarity ratio between the two triangles:

    17.5 / 40.25 = h / 28.75      (1)

We can solve the proportion for h by cross-multiplying:

    17.5 × 28.75 = 40.25 × h

    h = (17.5 × 28.75) / 40.25

    h = 12.5

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: The heights and shadows of similar objects are proportional. 

Let X be the height of the building that casts a shadow of length 28.75 under similar conditions.
So we have: 
   17.5 / 40.25 = X / 28.75
   
Cross-multiplying the above equation gives:
   17.5 x 28.75 = 40.25 X
   
Solving for X, we get:
   X = 17.5 x 28.75 / 40.25 = 12.5
   
Therefore, the height of the building is 12.5 meters.

H = (17.5 x 28.75) / 40.25

  The ratio of flagstaff height to shadow length is 17.5/40.25.
  Therefore, the ratio of building height to shadow length is H/L = 17.5/40.25.
  If the shadow length is 28.75, then we can solve for H: H=28.75*(17.5/40.25).
  Therefore H=12.5 meters.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 8:
Knowledge:
  The height and shadow length of an object are proportional to the height and shadow length of another object under similar conditions.
  Using the same proportionality constant k, we can write: 
    (Height of First Object) / (Shadow Length of First Object) = k
  and
    (Height of Second Object) / (Shadow Length of Second Object) = k
  
  We can find the value of the constant k by using the values given in the question:
    k = (Height of First Object) / (Shadow Length of First Object) = 17.5 / 40.25
  
  Once we have k, we can find the height of the second object using its shadow length:
    (Height of Second Object) / (Shadow Length of Second Object) = k
    (Height of Second Object) / 28.75 = (17.5 / 40.25)
Action: 
  We can simplify the above equation to find the height of the second object:
    (Height of Second Object) = (28.75 * 17.5) / 40.25 = 12.5
  Answer("B")

  B: 720
  C: 920
  D: None
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
This problem involves finding the number of permutations of 6 books. The formula for permutations is n!/(n-r)! where n is the total number of items and r is the number of items being selected.

Action: Answer("B")  
The total number of items is 6 and we are selecting all 6 items. Therefore, n=6 and r=6. Plugging this into the permutation formula:
6!/(6-6)! = 6!/0! = 6*5*4*3*2*1 = 720.
Thus, there are 720 ways to arrange the 6 books.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 20 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers?
Choices:
  A: (zy – 2x)/z
  B: (zy – 2)/z
  C: (zx – y)/(z – 2)
  D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2)
  E: (zy – x)/(z + 2)
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let a and b be the highest and lowest scores respectively.
  We know that (a + b)/2 = x, or a + b = 2x.
  Let s be the average score for the entire class excluding the highest and lowest scorers.
  We know that s = (total score - highest score - lowest score) / (z - 2).
  The total score for the class is y * z.
Action: Answer("D")  
To find s, we first need to find the total score - the sum of the highest and lowest score.
  The total score is yz. We already know the sum of the highest and lowest score is 2x. 
  So, the total score - the sum of the highest and lowest score is yz - 2x.
  Therefore, the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is:
  s = (yz - 2x) / (z - 2),
  which corresponds to answer choice D.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The average of the highest score and the lowest score is (highest + lowest) / 2 = (1/2) * (highest + lowest).
  - The average score for the entire class is the sum of all scores divided by the number of students.
  - To exclude the highest and lowest scorers, we need to subtract the highest and lowest scores from the sum of all scores before dividing by the number of remaining students, which is z - 2.
  - Formula: average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers = (sum of scores - highest - lowest) / (z - 2)
  
Solution:
  Let highest score = H, lowest score = L.
  It is given that (H + L) / 2 = x, so H + L = 2x.
  Also, let the sum of all scores be S.
  Then, S / z = y (given)
  S = yz
  We need to find (S - H - L) / (z - 2) in terms of x, y, and z.
  Substituting H + L = 2x, we get:
  (S - H - L) / (z - 2) = (yz - 2x) / (z - 2)
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  To find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scores, we need to find the sum of the scores of all the students except the highest and lowest scorers, and then divide that sum by the number of students excluding the highest and lowest scorers.
  If the average of the highest and lowest scores is x, and there are z students in the class, then the sum of the highest and lowest scores is 2xz.
  The average score for the class is y, so the sum of all the scores is yz.
  We need to find the sum of the scores of all the students except the highest and lowest scorers, which is yz - 2xz.
  The number of students excluding the highest and lowest scorers is z - 2.

Action: Answer("D")

  (yz - 2xz)/(z - 2). 
  Therefore, the answer is (zy – 2x)/(z - 2), which is choice (D).
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  Let A be the highest score, B be the lowest score,
  Then the arithmetic mean of A and B is (A+B)/2.
  We know that (A+B)/2 = x. 
  We want to find the average score of the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers, so we need to find the sum of all the scores except for the highest and the lowest, then divide by the number of scores.
  Number of scores = z - 2, since we are excluding the highest and lowest.
  Total score = y * z, since the average score for y and there are z students in the class.
  We can solve for A and B using the equation (A+B)/2 = x, which gives us A+B = 2x. 
  We substitute A = 2x - B into the equation Total score = A + B * (z - 2), which gives us Total score = (2x-B) + B(z-2) = 2x + B(z-4).
Action: Answer("D") 
  The sum of all the scores except for the highest and the lowest is Total score - A - B = 2x + B(z-4) - (2x + B) = B(z-4). 
  The average score excluding the highest and the lowest is (B(z-4)) / (z-2). 
  We can rewrite B as 2x - A as before, which gives us (2x - A)(z-4) / (z-2). 
  Substituting y*z for Total score and simplifying gives us (zy - 2x)/(z-2). Therefore, the correct answer is D.
Response 4:

  - The average score for the entire class is y. Therefore, the sum of all the students' scores is yz.
  - We are asked to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers.

  The sum of all the scores in the class is equal to the total number of students multiplied by the average score.
Action: Answer("D")  
The sum of all scores in the class is equal to the total number of students in the class multiplied by the average score of the class. Therefore, the average score of the class is (1/z) times the sum of all scores in the class.
Let a be the lowest score, b be the highest score, and s be the sum of scores of the remaining students. Then we have a + b = 2x, and s/(z-2) = y. Solving for s, we get s = (z-2)y. Therefore the sum of all scores is s + a + b = (z-2)y + 2x.

  highest value = lowest value + range
  lowest value = highest value - range

(a + b + s)/z = y
(2x - a + 2x - b + s)/z = y
(4x - (a + b) + s)/z = y
(4x - 2x + s)/z = y  [since a + b = 2x]
s/z = y - 2x/2 = y - x

Therefore, the total score of the remaining students (excluding the highest and lowest scorers) is y - x. The average score of these students is (y - x)/(z - 2).

(z - 2)y = (h + l + s)

(z - 2)y = 2x + s

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 23 of 100 ###

Question: At its maximum speed, a space shuttle can travel 700m high in 40 seconds. It will also take 5 seconds to pass a point. What then is the length of the space shuttle?

  A: 50 m
  B: 75 m
  C: 100 m
  D: 125 m
  E: 150 m
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Speed equals distance divided by time: speed = distance/time.
  To get the maximum speed, we need to use the first 40 seconds of travel.

Solution:
  The space shuttle travels 700 m in 40 seconds, so its speed is:
    v = distance / time = 700 / 40 = 17.5 m/s
    
  In the next 5 seconds, it travels an additional distance of:
    additional_distance = v * time = 17.5 * 5 = 87.5 m
    
  The total distance traveled in 45 seconds is:
    total_distance = 700 + 87.5 = 787.5 m
    
Action: Answer("E") The length of the space shuttle is 150 meters.

Response 8:
Knowledge: 
  The space shuttle has two stages of movement: 
  1. As it ascends vertically to a maximum height 
  2. As it moves horizontally, covering its length, L, in the remaining time.
  In the vertical stage, the space shuttle covers a distance, d, therefore the initial velocity, u_0, is 0m/s. The final velocity, V_f, when it reaches the maximum height is unknown. 
  The time taken in the vertical stage, t_v, is 40s. The acceleration due to gravity is -9.81m/s^2.  
  In the horizontal stage, the final velocity is known to be  L/(T-5) m/s, where T is the total time of flight.
  
  In order to get the length of the space shuttle, we need to find the time of flight T from the information given before.
  T = t_v + t_h, where t_h is the time taken for the horizontal stage of motion.
  We know that the initial velocity in the horizontal stage u_0 = V_f = L/t_h.
  We also know that the vertical displacement, d = 700m, is reached while the space shuttle is accelerating due to gravity. 
  Therefore,
  d = 1/2 *(-9.81) * t_v^2 
  
  We can use d to find V_f at the end of the vertical stage. 
  V_f = sqr(2*-9.81*d)
  
  From the above information, we can find t_h and thus L as follows:
  V_f = u_0 + a*t_h
  L = V_f *(T-5)
  
Action: Answer("C") 

We will substitute the appropriate values and equations to obtain the response.
d = 700m, t_v = 40s, a = -9.81m/s^2
t_h = T - t_v, u_0 = V_f = L/t_h

d = 1/2 *(-9.81)* t_v^2  => 700 = -19.62* 40^2 * 1/2 => t_v = ~20.07s

V_f = sqr(2*-9.81*d) => V_f = sqr(2*-9.81*700) => V_f = ~278.73m/s

V_f = u_0 + a*t_h => 278.73 = L/t_h + (-9.81)* (T-40) => Eqn1

L = V_f *(T-5)

Substitute the expression for L in eqn1:
=> 278.73 = [(V_f*(T-5))/t_h] + (-9.81)* (T-40) => Eqn2

Group both linear terms on the left-hand side:
=> 278.73 + 9.81*T = [(V_f*T)/t_h] + 9.81*5 + 278.73 -5V_f => Eqn3

Substitute the values of V_f, t_h, and t_v:
=> 278.73 + 9.81*T = [L/T] + 49.05 + 278.73 - 5[L/(T-5)] => Eqn4

Group the L terms on the right-hand side:
=> L[5/T(T-5)] + 9.81*T = [L/T] + 49.05 + 278.73 - [5L/T(T-5)] => Eqn5

Group the L terms on the left-hand side:
=> L[10/T(T-5)] = 327.78 - 9.81*T => Eqn6

Substitute T = 45 in Eqn6, to get L not considering units of measurements:
=> L = 100m.

Therefore, the length of the space shuttle is 100 meters. Answer("C")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 24 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. If the yard has an area of 240 square meters, how many meters of fencing does she need?
Choices:
  A: 58
  B: 62
  C: 66
  D: 70
  E: 74
Response 0:
Knowledge:
 1. The formula for the area of a rectangle is A = l x w, where l is the length and w is the width.
 2. The perimeter of a rectangle is given by P = 2l + 2w, where l is the length and w is the width.

Action: 
Let x be the width of the yard in meters.
From the given information, the length of the yard is (240/x) meters.
Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides, which is equivalent to one length and two widths minus the 10 meters unfenced side, so the amount of fencing required is 2((240/x)+x)-10 meters.
Simplifying the above expression, we get (480/x) + 2x - 10 meters.
To get the value of x, we must solve the equation 240 = x((240/x)+x).
Simplifying the above expression, we get x^2 + 240/x - 240 = 0.
Factoring the above expression, we get (x + 20)(x - 12) = 0.
Since the width cannot be negative, then x = 12 meters.is the width of the yard.
The length of the yard, in this case, would be 20 meters.
Substituting the value of x into the expression for fencing, we get 2((240/12)+12)-10 = 62 meters.
Answer: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  When a rectangular yard has one side unfenced, the yard has a width w and length l, and the area is A, then:
  A = w * l
  The length of fencing required is L = 2w + l
  If we know the values of two of the variables A, w, l, we can solve for the third.

Solution:
  Let w and l be the width and length of her rectangular yard, in meters. 
  Area of the yard = w * l = 240
  One side is 10 meters unfenced, so the fencing is required for three sides, each of length l + w, with one side of length 10 left alone.
  Hence the fencing required = 2l + 2w = 3(l + w) - 10.
  Through this, we can form two equations:
  (1) A = wl = 240.
  (2) 2l + 2w = 3(l + w) - 10.
  Simplifying equation (2), we get:
  2l + 2w = 3l + 3w - 10.
  l + w = 10 + 240/3 = 90/3 + 240/3 = 330/3 = 110.
  Therefore, w = 110 - l.
  Plugging w = 110 - l into equation (1), we get:
  l(110 - l) = 240.
  Simplifying and solving for l, we get:
  l^2 - 110l + 240 = 0.
  Factoring:
  (l-10)(l-100) = 0.
  Therefore, l = 10 or l = 100, but l ≠ 10 because that would imply w = 100 and her yard would not be rectangular.
  l = 100 is the only valid option, so w = 110 - l = 10.
  Total fencing length required = 2l + 2w = 220 + 20 = 240 meters.

Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge:

  Solving for W gives: 
  W^2 - (P-10)W + 2A = 0.

  W^2 - 2LW - 10W + 480 = 0.
  Since we know that W is a factor of 480, we can find that the possible values of W are {10, 12, 16, 30}.
  However, only the value of W = 12 meters gives us a positive value for L and a correct total perimeter P = 46 meters.

Action:

- The total length of fencing she needs is the sum of the three sides, which is 2y + x + 10. 
- Substituting y, we get 2((240 - 10x)/x) + x + 10 = 2(240/x - 10) + x + 10.
- We want to find x, so we can take the derivative of this expression and set it to 0 to find the minimum point. After doing so, we find that x ≈ 16.33.
- Therefore, y = (240 - 10x) / x ≈ 13.96.
- Finally, the total length of fencing she needs is 2y + x + 10 ≈ 60.28.

Response 4:
Knowledge: 
  If we let `a` be the length of the yard and `b` be the width of the yard, then the area of the yard is given by  `a * b`.
  The perimeter of the yard is the sum of the lengths of all the sides, which is `a + b + a + 10 + b`.
  We are given that the area of the yard is 240 square meters, which means that `a * b = 240`.

Solution: 
  We know that `a * b = 240`.
  We want to find the perimeter of the yard, which is `a + b + a + 10 + b = 2a + 2b + 10`.
  We can use the fact that `a * b = 240` to solve for one of the variables (for example, `a = 240 / b`), and then substitute that into the expression for the perimeter to get an equation in terms of just one variable.
  
  Substituting `a = 240 / b` into the expression for the perimeter, we get:

    2a + 2b + 10 = 2(240/b) + 2b + 10

  Simplifying that expression gives:

    2a + 2b + 10 = (480 + 2b^2) / b + 10

  Setting the perimeter equal to a variable `p`, we can solve for `b`:

    p = (480 + 2b^2) / b + 10
    pb = 480 + 2b^2 + 10b
    2b^2 + 10b - pb + 480 = 0
    
  Using the quadratic formula with `a=2`, `b=10`, and `c=-pb+480`, we get:

    b = (-10 ± sqrt(100 + 8pb - 960)) / 4
    b = (-5 ± sqrt(pb - 80)) / 2

  We know that `b` must be positive (since it represents a length), so we take the positive root:

    b = (-5 + sqrt(pb - 80)) / 2

  Now we can use this value of `b` to find `a`:

    a = 240 / b

  And finally, we can calculate the perimeter:

    p = 2a + 2b + 10

Solution2:
  Alternatively, we can solve for `a` using the equation for the area (`a * b = 240`), and then substitute that into the expression for the perimeter:

    a * b = 240
    a = 240 / b

    p = 2a + 2b + 10
    p = 480/b + 2b + 10

  Now we have an expression for the perimeter in terms of just one variable, `b`. We can take the derivative of this expression with respect to `b`, set it equal to zero to find the minimum value of `p`, and then solve for `b`.

  dp/db = -480/b^2 + 2 = 0
  480/b^2 = 2
  b^2 = 240
  b = sqrt(240) ≈ 15.49

  Finally, we can use this value of `b` to find `a` and the perimeter:

    a = 240 / b ≈ 15.49
    p = 2a + 2b + 10 ≈ 62.96

  Since the length of the rectangle cannot be smaller than the width of 10 meters, we have L = 100.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 25 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A sporting goods store carries only yellow and white golf balls. At the beginning of the day it had 600 golf balls in stock, and by the end of the day it had sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls. If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, and in doing so sold all of its white golf balls, how many yellow golf balls did the store have to begin the day?
Choices:
  A: 80
  B: 120
  C: 240
  D: 320
  E: 360
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - The store sells out all of its white golf balls
  - The store sells an equal number of yellow and white golf balls.
  - The store has only yellow and white golf balls in stock.
  
Let x be the original number of each color.

By the end of the day, 80% of the total number of golf balls were sold. Hence, the store sold 0.8(2x) golf balls.

We know that the store sold all of its white golf balls. Therefore, 

white golf balls sold = amount of white golf balls in the inventory = x

We can find the number of yellow golf balls in the inventory using the fact that yellow golf balls sold equals the white golf balls sold:

yellow golf balls sold = white golf balls sold = x

The total golf balls in the inventory can be written as:

Total number of golf balls in inventory = number of yellow balls + number of white balls = 2x

Therefore:

yellow golf balls in inventory = total golf balls in inventory - white golf balls in inventory
                                    = 2x - x
                                    = x

The percentage of total golf balls sold can be computed using the following formula:

percentage of total golf balls sold = (number of golf balls sold / initial number of golf balls) * 100

We substitute the known values to get:

80 = (0.8(2x) / (2x)) * 100

We simplify to get:

80 = 40/x

x = 40/0.8 = 50

Action: Answer("E")

  - The store sold 80% of its 600 golf balls, which means it sold 0.8 x 600 = 480 golf balls.
  - Half of the sold golf balls were white, which means the store sold 480/2 = 240 white golf balls.
  - The store had to begin the day with the same number of yellow golf balls as white golf balls that it sold, which is 240.

Topic: Math
Question: The bus fare for two persons for travelling between Agra and Aligarh id four-thirds the train fare between the same places for one person. The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512. Find the train fare between the two places for one person?
Choices:
  A: 126
  B: 77
  C: 88
  D: 66
  E: 54
Response 0:
Let X be the train fare for one person.
Given that the bus fare for two persons is four-thirds the train fare for one person.
Hence, the bus fare for 1 person is 2/3 times the train fare for 1 person.
Hence, the total fare for 6 persons travelling by bus between the two places is (2/3)*4*X*3 = 8X
And the total fare for 8 persons travelling by train between the same places is 8X.

The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512. 
Hence, 6(8X) + 8(8X) = 1512
Solving this equation gives X = 88

Therefore, the answer is option C: 88.
Response 1:
Let train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person be x.
Then, bus fare for two persons for the same distance = (4/3)*x

Total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus = 3*(4/3)*x = 4x
Total fare paid by 8 persons travelling by train = 8x

Given, the total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512.
Hence, 4x + 8x = 1512
12x = 1512
x = 126

Therefore, the train fare between Agra and Aligarh for one person is Rs.126.

  We know that the sum of the number of persons travelling by bus and train is 6+8=14

- The fare paid by 8 persons travelling by train = 8T
- The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train = 12B + 8T = Rs. 1512

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 27 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Jim filled his dog's bowl with dog food. Starting at 8:00 am, Jim's dog ate exactly once an hour, consuming exactly 1/3 of the dog food remaining in the bowl at each feeding session. Approximately, what percent of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon of the same day?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 25%
  C: 30%
  D: 35%
  E: 40%
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Starting at 8:00 am, the dog ate every hour until noon, meaning 4 times it was fed.
  Each feeding session the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining dog food in the bowl.
  
Calculations:
  Let F be the amount of dog food when the dog started eating.
  After the first feeding session, there is 2/3 of F in the bowl.
  After the second feeding session, there is (2/3) * (2/3) * F = (4/9) F in the bowl.
  After the third feeding session, there is (2/3) * (4/9) * F = (8/27) F in the bowl.
  After the fourth feeding session, there is (2/3) * (8/27) * F = (16/81) F in the bowl.
  Therefore, just before the noon feedings session, there was (16/81) F amount of dog food in the bowl.

  Now to calculate the percentage of the original food, we can have:
  (16/81) F / F * 100% = 19.75%, which is approximately 20%.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  If the dog eats $\frac{1}{3}$ of what was in the bowl at each feeding session, two-thirds of the food remain each time.
  From 8:00 am to noon there are 4 hours and therefore 4 feeding sessions.

Solution:
  With each feeding session, two-thirds of the food remains. Therefore, the amount of the original food that was left before the first feeding session is $\frac{2}{3}$ of the original food. This is because the dog ate 1/3 of the original food before the first feeding session.  After the first feeding session, the amount of food remaining is $\frac{2}{3}$ of that amount. That is,
  $\frac{2}{3}\cdot \frac{2}{3} = \frac{4}{9}$
  of the original food remains after two feeding sessions. Similarly, after three feeding sessions, we have
  $\frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} = \frac{8}{27}$.
  And after four feeding session (i.e., before the dog began to eat at noon), we have
  $\frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3} = \frac{16}{81}$.
  Therefore, the approximate percentage of the original food in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon is
  $\frac{16}{81} \approx 19.8\% \approx 20\%$.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 28 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Anna is able to buy 5 more articles for $300 after the price of each article decreased by 15%. What is the new selling price of each article?
Choices:
  A: $8
  B: $10
  C: $13.6
  D: $22.9
  E: $40
Response 0:
Knowledge:
To solve the problem, we can find the original price of the articles first, then use that to calculate the new price after the discount.
If the price decreased by 15%, then the new price is 85% of the original price.
We also know that Anna can buy 5 more articles for $300, so the original price of each article is $300/(5+5) = $30.

Calculation:
New price = 85% of $30
New price = 0.85 x $30
New price = $25.5

Anna can buy 10 articles for $300, so:
New selling price of each article = $300/10
New selling price of each article = $30

Anna's new selling price of each article after discount is $25.5, which is close to $25.
Action: Answer("None of the Above") 
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  If Anna can buy 5 more articles and pay $300 in total, and she has increased her purchasing power by 5/0.85 = 5.88 times. 
  Thus the original cost of 1 article is $300/5.88=$51.
  The decrease of price was 15%, so the new price is $51*0.85=$<b>43.35</b>.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  - The original total price of the articles is 5p where p is the original price of each article.
  - The new total price of the articles is $300, which is 0.85(5p), after every article gets a 15% discount.
  - $300 is $75 less than 5p.
  - Therefore, p=$75/5=$15.
Action: Answer("$12.75") 
  - The new price of each article is 85% of $15. 
  - 0.85($15)=$12.75.
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  1. Anna buys more articles after the price decreases by 15%.
  2. If the price of one article is decreased by 15%, the new price is 100-15= 85% of the original price.
  3. The total amount Anna pays ($300) is equal to the new price of each article multiplied by the number of articles she bought.
  4. Anna can buy 5 more articles after the price decreased.
 
Calculation:
  Let the original price of one article be x.
  After the reduction of 15%, the new price of one article is 0.85*x.
  Anna can buy for $300 total, so we have (0.85*x + 5)*(N articles) = $300
  Substitute N = (total articles before) + 5
  We will obtain an equation in x that we can solve.

    (0.85*x + 5)(N) = $300
    (0.85*x + 5)((total articles before) + 5) = $300
    (0.85*x + 5)(total articles before) = $250
    0.85*x(total articles before) + 5(total articles before) = $250
    0.85*x(total articles before) = $250- 5(total articles before)
    x = (250- 5(total articles before))/ (0.85(total articles before)) = (294-5(total articles before))/17(total articles before)

Question: A rope 20 meters long is cut into two pieces. If the length of one piece of rope is 3 meters shorter than the length of the other, what is the length, in meters, of the longer piece of rope?
Choices:
  A: 7.5
  B: 8.9
  C: 9.9
  D: 11.5
  E: 11.7
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let x be the length of the longer piece of rope and y be the length of the shorter piece of rope. 
  We know that the sum of the lengths of the two pieces of rope is equal to 20 meters.
  So, we have x + y = 20.
  We also know that the length of one piece of rope is 3 meters shorter than the other:
  x = y + 3.
  We can use substitution to solve for y.
  Substituting y + 3 for x in x + y = 20, we get:
  (y + 3) + y = 20
  2y + 3 = 20
  2y = 17
  y = 8.5
  Then, we can use the equation x = y + 3 to find x:
  x = 8.5 + 3 = 11.5

Question: In a survey of students, each student selected from a list of 10 songs the 2 songs that the student liked best. If each song was selected 5 times, how many students were surveyed?
Choices:
  A: 96
  B: 48
  C: 32
  D: 25
  E: 18
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If each song was selected 5 times, then there must be a total of 10*5=50 selections.
  In each selection, a student chose 2 songs, so the total number of selections is also equal to twice the number of students surveyed.
  Therefore, the number of students surveyed is 50 / 2 = 25.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Each song was selected 5 times by the surveyed students.
  We can use the formula n = N / r, where N is the total number of selections and r is the number of selections for each individual.
  In this case, N = 10 x 5 = 50 (total number of selections), and r = 2 (number of selections for each student).
  So, n = 50 / 2 = 25.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 31 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The original retail price of an appliance was 60 percent more than its wholesale cost. If the appliance was actually sold for 20 percent less than the original retail price, then it was sold for what percent more than its wholesale cost?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 28%
  C: 36%
  D: 40%
  E: 42%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let the wholesale cost be X.
  Then the original retail price was (100+60)%=160% of X.
  And the actual selling price was (100-20)%=80% of the original retail price.

Calculation:
  The actual selling price was (80/100)*160% of X, which simplifies to 128% of X.
  So the appliance was sold for 128% of the wholesale cost, which is 28% more than the wholesale cost.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume that the wholesale cost is 100 dollars. Then, the original retail price would be 160 dollars since it is 60% more than the wholesale cost. After that, the appliance was sold for 20% less than the original retail price, which is (1 - 20/100) = 0.8 times the original price.
  To calculate the final percentage increase:
  1. First, we calculate the difference between the original retail price and the sale price.
  2. Then, we divide that difference by the wholesale cost.
  3. After that, we multiply the result by 100 to express it as a percentage.
  4. Finally, we take the absolute value of the result because we want to know the percent increase, regardless of whether the sale price is greater than the original retail price.

Working: 
  1. The difference between the original retail price and the sale price is:
  160 - (160 * 0.8) = 160 - 128 = 32
  2. We divide that by the wholesale cost to get:
  32 / 100 = 0.32
  3. We multiply that by 100 to get: 
  0.32 * 100 = 32%
  4. Finally, we take the absolute value to get the percent increase: 
  |32| = 32

Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  Let W be the wholesale cost of the appliance.
  The original retail price of an appliance is 60% more than its wholesale cost, so it is 1.6W.
  The appliance is actually sold for 20% less than the original retail price, so it is sold for 0.8(1.6W)=1.28W.
  The percent increase over its wholesale cost is (1.28W - W)/W x 100% = 28%, so the correct answer is B.
Action: Answer("B")

  The percent increase in selling price compared to the wholesale cost is the difference between the selling price and the wholesale cost divided by the wholesale cost.
  So, the percent increase in the selling price is ((1.28W - W) / W) * 100 = 28%.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 32 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: When folded into two equal halves a rectangular sheet had a perimeter of 48cm for each part folded along one set of sides and the same is 66cm when folded along the other set of sides. Find the area of the sheet.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 1120
  C: 792
  D: 1320
  E: 1200
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  When a rectangular sheet is folded in half along one set of sides, the perimeter of each part will be half the perimeter of the original sheet.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is equal to two times the length plus two times the breadth.
  The area of a rectangle is equal to the product of its length and breadth.
  
Solution:
  Let the length and breadth of the sheet be L and B respectively.
  When folded along the length, we have:
  2(L/2 + B) = 48
  L + 2B = 48               (1)
  
  When folded along the breadth, we have:
  2(L + B/2) = 66
  2L + B = 66               (2)

  Solving the above two equations simultaneously, we get:
  L = 18 cm
  B = 15 cm       

  Area of the sheet = LB = 18 x 15 = 270 cm^2

Answer: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  When we fold a paper by half along one set of sides, we are effectively halving the length of that side. The same is true for the other set of sides.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by the sum of the length of all 4 sides of a rectangle.
  The area of a rectangle is given by the product of the length and width of a rectangle.
  
Action: 
Let's say the length of the sheet is "l" and the width is "w". 
When folded along the length, each part has a perimeter of 48/2 = 24cm, which means the length of each part is (24/2) - w. 
When folded along the width, each part has a perimeter of 66/2 = 33cm, which means the width of each part is (33/2) - l.
We can set up two equations using the above information:

2l + 2(2w - 24) = 48
2w + 2(2l - 33) = 66

Solving these two equations gives us l = 21 and w = 15.

Now that we know the length and width of the rectangle, we can find its area as:
Area = l * w = 21 * 15 = 315

Answer: Answer("None of the above"). The correct answer is 315, which is not one of the given choices.
Response 2:
Let the dimensions of the rectangle be l and w, where l is the longer side and w is the shorter side. When folded along the longer side, each part has a perimeter of 48cm, so its length is 24cm. Thus, the longer side of the rectangle is 2 * 24 = 48 cm. Similarly, when folded along the shorter side, each part has a perimeter of 66cm, so its width is 33cm. Thus, the shorter side of the rectangle is 2 * 33 = 66 cm. The area of the sheet is l * w = 48 * 66 = 3168 sq. cm. 

Action: Answer("None of the above") 

(Note: None of the choices match our calculated answer of 3168 sq. cm.)
Response 3:
Let l and w be the length and width of the rectangular sheet.
When folded along the length, each part has a length of l/2 and a width of w, and the total perimeter of the folded parts is 66cm. Therefore:
2(l/2 + w) = 66
l + 2w = 66
l = 66 - 2w
When folded along the width, each part has a length of l and a width of w/2, and the total perimeter of the folded parts is 48cm. Therefore:
2(l + w/2) = 48
2l + w = 48
Now substitute l = 66 - 2w into the second equation:
2(66 - 2w) + w = 48
132 - 3w = 48
3w = 84
w = 28
l = 66 - 2w = 10
The area of the rectangular sheet is lw = 10 x 28 = 280 cm^2.
Therefore the answer is A: 1584. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 4:
Solution:
Let the length and the breadth of the sheet be 'l' and 'b', respectively. When folded along the length, each half has a perimeter of 48 cm. So, 2(l/2 + b) = 48. Therefore, l + 2b = 48. When folded along the breadth, each half has a perimeter of 66 cm. So, 2(l + b/2) = 66. Therefore, 2l + b = 66.
We can solve these two equations to get l = 24 cm and b = 9 cm.
The area of the sheet is l * b = 24 * 9 = 216 sq cm.
When we fold the rectangular sheet, we get two equal halves. So the area of each half is (1/2) * (l * b) = (1/2) * 216 = 108 sq cm.
Therefore, the answer is 108 sq cm * 2 = 216 sq cm.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 5:
Knowledge:
  When a rectangular sheet of length 'l' and breath 'b' is folded along its length, the perimeter becomes '2l+2b'
  When a rectangular sheet of length 'l' and breath 'b' is folded along its breadth, the perimeter becomes '2l+2b'
  We can get two equations from the above statements and solve them to get the values of 'l' and 'b'
  
Calculations:
  Let's assume length = 'l' and breadth = 'w' of the rectangular sheet.
  
  When folded along length => 2l + w = 48/2 = 24 => Equation 1: 2l + w = 24
  
  When folded along breadth => l + 2w = 66/2 = 33 => Equation 2: l + 2w = 33
  
  Solving the above equations, we can find that l = 15, w = 9
  
  Therefore, area of the rectangular sheet = l*w = 15*9 = 135
  
Action: Answer("E")
Response 6:
Knowledge: 
  When folded along one set of sides, each part will have a length and a width that add up to half of the perimeter. Similarly, when folded along the other set of sides, each part will have a length and a width that add up to the other half of the perimeter. The area of the rectangular sheet can be found by multiplying the length and width together.

Let's work through the problem:
Let's denote the length as l and the width as w. Then we know that:
  2l + 2w = 48  =>  l + w = 24
  2l + 2w = 66  =>  l + w = 33

Subtracting the first equation from the second equation gives:
  33 - 24 = l => l = 9

Substituting l back into either of the first two equations gives:
  w = 24 - l => w = 15

Therefore, the area of the sheet is:
  A = l * w = 9 * 15 = 135  

Action: Answer("E")
Response 7:
Knowledge: 
  - When a rectangular sheet is folded into two equal halves along its length, the perimeter of each part will reduce by half.
  - Hence, if the original perimeter is P, then when folded along its length, the new perimeter will be P/2.
  - When a rectangular sheet is folded into two equal halves along its breadth, the length of each part will be reduced by half.
  - Hence, if the original perimeter is P, then when folded along its breadth, the new perimeter will be P/2 + 2B (where B is the breadth of the sheet).
  - Also, since the length of each part is reduced by half, the new breadth will be double that of the original breadth.
  - We can use the above two facts to form two equations and solve for length and breadth of the original sheet.
  - After we find the length and breadth, the area of the original sheet can be calculated as L x B.

Action: 
  Let L and B be the length and breadth of the rectangular sheet.
  From the problem, we have two equations: 
  2(L+B) = 48  ... equation 1 (when folded along length)
  L + 2(2B) + 2(L-B) = 66  ... equation 2 (when folded along breadth)
  Simplifying equation 2: 2L + 2B = 33   ... equation 3
  Subtracting equation 3 from equation 1: L - 2B = 9   ... equation 4
  Adding equation 3 and equation 4: 3L = 42,  so L = 14.
  Substituting L = 14 in equation 4: 14 - 2B = 9, so B = 2.5.
  Therefore, the area of the original sheet is L x B = 14 x 2.5 = 35 sq.cm.
  Answer: None of the Above (The calculated area is not one of the choices)
Response 8:
Knowledge: 
  When a rectangular sheet is folded into two equal halves:
  - The length of one part is equal to the width of the other part.
  - The perimeter of one part is equal to the perimeter of the other part.
  - The area of the sheet is equal to twice the product of the length and the width.

Let L and W be the length and width of the sheet, respectively.
Then two equations can be formed from the given information:
- 2L + W = 48
- 2W + L = 66

Solving for L and W:
- L = (48 - W)/2
- L = 66 - 2W

Substituting the first equation into the second:
- (48 - W)/2 = 66 - 2W
- 48 - W = 132 - 4W
- 3W = 84
- W = 28

Substituting W = 28 into the first equation:
- 2L + 28 = 48
- 2L = 20
- L = 10

Therefore, the area of the sheet is:
- A = 2LW = 2(10)(28) = 560

  - If Bill's usual speed is 15 mph, then his speed on a windy day is 15 - 4 = 11 mph.

Calculation:
  - distance = speed * time = 11 * 0.35 = 3.85 miles

Topic: Math
Question: In a bag of red and green sweets, the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4. If the bag contains 120 green sweets, how many red sweets are there?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 80
  C: 95
  D: 100
  E: 85
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  We know that the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4. This means if we divide the total number of sweets into 7 equal parts, 3 parts will be red sweets and 4 parts will be green sweets. 
  We are given that there are 120 green sweet in the bag.

Action: First, we need to find out how many sweets are there in total. We can set up a proportion here:
  4/7 = 120/T
  Cross multiplying we get T = 120*7/4 = 210
  So, there are 210 sweets in the bag.
  Now we can use the ratio of red sweets to green sweets to find the number of red sweets:
  If there are 7 parts in total, and 4 of them are green, then 3 of them are red.
  So, the number of red sweets is (3/7)*210 = 90.

Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
To solve this question we can use the fact that the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4. This means that for every 3 red sweets there are 4 green sweets. We are also told that the bag contains 120 green sweets.
Action: 
Let's start by using the ratio to find the number of red sweets. We can set up a proportion as follows:
3/4 = x/120
Here, x represents the number of red sweets.
To solve for x, we can cross-multiply and simplify:
4x = 3*120
4x = 360
x = 90
Therefore, there are 90 red sweets in the bag.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 35 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A number of friends decided to go on a picnic and planned to spend Rs. 96 on eatables. Four of them, however, did not turn up. As a consequence, the remaining ones had to contribute Rs. 4 extra, each. The number of those who attended the picnic was
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 12
  C: 16
  D: 24
  E: 25
Response 0:
Let's assume that the total number of friends was "x". The total amount they planned to spend was Rs. 96. Therefore, the amount each friend would pay initially would be 96/x. But since 4 friends did not show up, the amount each person had to pay increased by Rs. 4. Therefore, each of the remaining (x-4) friends would have to pay Rs. 4 extra, making it (96/x + 4) each. We know that (x-4) people paid this amount. So, we can set up the following equation to solve for x: 

96/x = 96/x + 4 * (x-4)

Solving for x, we get x = 16 
Therefore, the number of those who attended the picnic was 16.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
Let's assume that there were n people originally and they spent Rs. x on eatables, Therefore, the actual cost per person was (x/n) and the revised cost/person after 4 people didn't turn up is (x/n+4).
According to the problem:
    n-4 people paid (x/n+4) each
    Total cost is still x.
    Total cost = (n-4) * (x/n+4) + 4 * (x/n) = x
    Therefore we can solve this equation for n.

Action: Answer("C") 
Solution:
    (n-4) * (x/n+4) + 4 * (x/n) = x
    Expanding the equation
    nx + 16n - 4x - 16 = nx
    Solving for n
    n = 16
Therefore, the number of people that attended the picnic was 16.

96 + 4N - 384/N - 16 = 96

Simplifying and rearranging:
4N^2 - 96N - 384 = 0

Dividing both sides by 4:
N^2 - 24N - 96 = 0

Using the quadratic formula:
N = (24 ± sqrt(24^2 + 4*96)) / 2
N = (24 ± sqrt(768)) / 2
N = (24 ± 24√3) / 2

Ignoring the negative root, we get:
N = 12 + 12√3

Therefore, the number of friends who attended the picnic was approximately 12 + 12√3.

Response 5:
Let the number of friends initially planned to go on the picnic be "x".
Their contribution towards the picnic was Rs.96.
Thus, each friend was supposed to pay 96/x Rs.

Thus, total money collected now = remaining friends * (96/x + 4) Rs.
This should be equal to the total money that was initially planned to be spent i.e. 96 Rs.

Response 6:
Let x be the number of friends that initially planned to attend the picnic, and y be the amount each was supposed to contribute. The total amount to be contributed is xy, which is Rs. 96.
When four of them did not turn up, the number of friends who attended the picnic was x - 4. The amount each had to pay increased to y + 4, and the total amount collected became (x-4)(y+4). According to the problem, this amount was also Rs. 96, so we have the equation:

    (x-4)(y+4) = 96

Expanding the left side of this equation, we get:

    xy - 4x + 4y - 16 = 96

Substituting xy = 96, we get:

    96 - 4x + 4y - 16 = 96

Collecting like terms, we obtain:

    4y - 4x = 16

Simplifying, we get:

    y - x = 4

We know that the number of friends who attended the picnic was x - 4, and the amount each had to pay was y + 4. Since xy = 96, we can write:

    (x-4)(y+4) = 96
   
Substituting y - x = 4, we get:

   (x-4)(x+8) = 96
   
Expanding the left side of this equation, we obtain:

   x^2 + 4x - 128 = 0
   
Solving this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula, we obtain:

   x = 8 or x = -16

Since x represents the number of friends, which must be a positive integer, we reject the solution x = -16. Therefore, the number of friends who attended the picnic was x - 4 = 8 - 4 = 4.

We can equate these two together, which will give us an equation to solve for x.

Calculation: 
Initial cost:    xa = 96  (total amount 'a' multiplied by the number of friends 'x')
Cost after changes: (x-4)*(a+4)

Equating both, we get:
96 = (x-4)*(a+4)
96 = (x-4) * (96/x + 4)

Simplifying this equation:
96 = 96 + 4x - 384/x - 16
4x - 16 = 384/x
4(x-4) = 384/x
x^2 - 4x - 96 = 0

Using the quadratic formula, we get:
x = 12 or x = -8. Discarding the negative value, we get the number of friends who attended the picnic was:

Action: Answer("B") 
Response 9:
Let the total number of friends that planned to go to the picnic be x. 
If four did not turn up, the number of friends who did turn up is x-4. 

Each of them had to contribute Rs. 4 extra, therefore the total amount they needed to contribute was 96 + (4 * (x - 4)) = 4x + 80.

We know that the total amount they actually spent was Rs. 96. 

Equating the two amounts we can find the value of x: 

4x + 80 = 96
4x = 16
x = 4

Since x is 20, the number of friends who attended the picnic is x-4 = 16. 

Answer: Answer("C")

Question: there are more than 501 students in a school such that 20% of them exactly took physics and 28% of them exactly took math. What could be the least possible no of students in the school?
Choices:
  A: 550
  B: 570
  C: 600
  D: 700
  E: none of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
* 20% of students took physics, so the number of students that took physics is 0.2x, where x is the total number of students.
* 28% of students took math, so the number of students that took math is 0.28x, where x is the total number of students.
* The total number of students is greater than 501.

Calculation:
* Let's start by assuming there are 550 total students in the school, then the number of students taking physics is 0.2 * 550 = 110, and the number of students taking math is 0.28 * 550 = 154. The total number of students taking either physics or math is 110 + 154 = 264, which is less than 501. So, we can eliminate option A.
* Next, if we assume that there are 570 total students in the school, then the number of students taking physics is 0.2 * 570 = 114, and the number of students taking math is 0.28 * 570 = 159. The total number of students taking either physics or math is 114 + 159 = 273, which is still less than 501. So, we can eliminate option B.
* If we assume that there are 600 total students in the school, then the number of students taking physics is 0.2 * 600 = 120, and the number of students taking math is 0.28 * 600 = 168. The total number of students taking either physics or math is 120 + 168 = 288, which is still less than 501. So, we can eliminate option C.
* If we assume that there are 700 total students in the school, then the number of students taking physics is 0.2 * 700 = 140, and the number of students taking math is 0.28 * 700 = 196. The total number of students taking either physics or math is 140 + 196 = 336, which is greater than 501. Therefore, the least possible number of students is 700.

Action: Answer("D")
