Question: Fernando purchased a university meal plan that allows him to have a total of 3 lunches and 3 dinners per week. If the cafeteria is closed on weekends and Fernando always goes home for a dinner on Friday nights, how many options does he have to allocate his meals?
Choices:
  A: 5C3*4C3
  B: 5C4*4C2
  C: 5C2*4C4
  D: 5C6*4C5
  E: 4C3*4C3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Fernando has 3 lunch and 3 dinner meal options to allocate each week.
  He goes home Friday nights, and so he has to have dinner on Fridays there.
  This leaves him with allocating 2 dinners and 3 lunches.
  The number of ways to choose k items from a set of n items is denoted by nCk.
  
Action: Answer("5C2*4C2")  
Explanation: Fernando has to choose 2 dinners out of the 4 remaining dinner options, which is 4C2, and he has to choose 3 lunches from the 5 remaining lunch options, which is 5C3. Therefore, the total number of plan options is 5C3 * 4C2, which is answer B.
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
We want to know how many options Fernando has to allocate his meals. He has 3 lunches and 3 dinners that he can have on weekdays, but only 2 dinners that he has to have on weekdays; one of them is on Friday because he goes home. Therefore, he has to choose 2 out of the remaining 3 days of the weekdays to have dinner. He can have lunch on any of the remaining weekdays. 
We have to calculate the number of ways Fernando can choose his meals. 
  A: If we choose 3 out of 5 weekdays for lunch and 3 out of 4 weekdays for dinner, we might accidentally count Friday, which is not an option for a weekday dinner. 
  B: If we choose 4 out of 5 weekdays for lunch and 2 out of 4 weekdays for dinner, we can guarantee that we don't choose Friday for a weekday dinner. Therefore, Fernando has 5C4 options for weekday lunches and 4C2 options for weekday dinners. 
  C: If we choose 2 out of 5 weekdays for lunch and 4 out of 4 weekdays for dinner, we force Fernando to have no weekday lunch at all, which is not allowed by the problem. 
  D: If we choose 6 out of 5 weekdays for lunch and 5 out of 4 weekdays for dinner, we force Fernando to have more meals than he paid for, which is not allowed by the problem. 
  E: If we choose 3 out of 4 weekdays for lunch and 3 out of 4 weekdays for dinner, we may accidentally choose Friday for a weekday dinner. 
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Since the cafeteria is closed on weekends and Fernando always misses one dinner, he has to allocate 5 meals (3 lunches and 2 dinners) in  the weekdays.
  To count the number of ways he can allocate his meals, we need to use combinations.
  The formula to find the number of ways to choose k items from a set of n items is: nCk = n! / [ k! * (n - k)! ], where n! represents n factorial, meaning the product of all positive integers up to n.
  
Analysis: 
  Fernando has 5 meals to allocate in the weekdays: 3 lunches and 2 dinners.
  He can choose 3 lunches out of 5 in 5C3 ways.
  He can choose 2 dinners out of 2 in 1 way (since he always goes home on Friday nights).
  Therefore, he only needs to select 1 dinner of the remaining 3 meals.
  Hence, he can choose 1 dinner out of 3 in 3C1 ways.
  The total number of options to allocate his meals is the product of these three values: 5C3 * 1 * 3C1 = 5*4*3 / 3*2*1 * 3 = 20.
  Therefore, the answer is 20, which is not among the choices.
  To find the closest alternative, we can simplify the expression 5C3 * 1 * 3C1
  5C3 = 5C2 = 5! / ( 2! * 3!) = 10
  3C1 = 3
  5C2 * 3 = 10 * 3 = 30.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 74 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: π
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: π
  E: 8:3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The volume of a cube of edge length "a" is given by V_cube = a^3
  - The volume of a sphere of radius "r" is given by V_sphere = 4/3 π r^3
  
Analysis:
  We need to compare the volumes of the cube and the sphere that would fit inside it as snugly as possible. Since the sphere fits snugly inside the cube, the diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge length of the cube. Let "a" be the edge length of the cube. The diameter of the sphere will be "a" as well, so its radius will be r = a/2. Now, we can calculate the ratio of volumes:

  V_cube/V_sphere = (a^3) / ((4/3) π (a/2)^3)
                  = 3a^3 / (4 π a^3 / 8)
                  = (3/2) (8/4π)
                  = 6/π

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The volume of a cube with side length 'a' is a^3.
  - The volume of a sphere with radius 'r' is (4/3)πr^3.
  - If a sphere fits inside a cube, the diameter of the sphere is equal to the side length of the cube.
  
To find the ratio of the volume of the cube to the volume of the sphere, we need to find the side length of the cube in terms of the radius of the sphere. 

Let the radius of the sphere be r. The diameter of the sphere is 2r. Since the sphere fits inside the cube, the side length of the cube is 2r. Therefore, the volume of the cube is (2r)^3 = 8r^3 and the volume of the sphere is (4/3)πr^3. The ratio of the volumes is: 

(8r^3)/((4/3)πr^3) = (6/π)

Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The volume of a cube is given by V_cube = s^3 where s is the length of a side of the cube.
  The volume of a sphere is given by V_sphere = 4/3 * π * r^3 where r is the radius of the sphere.
  If the diameter of the sphere is equal to the side length of the cube, then the sphere will fit perfectly inside the cube. 
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the diagonal of the cube, so d=s*√3.
  
Analysis:
  Let's assume that the side length of the cube and the diameter of the sphere are equal, then:
  V_cube = s^3
  V_sphere = 4/3 * π * (s/2)^3 = 4/3 * π * s^3/8 = π * s^3/6
  So, the ratio of the volumes is:
  V_cube : V_sphere = s^3 : π * s^3/6 = 6 : π

  Simplifying, we get V_sphere = (1/6)πa^3
  The ratio of the volumes is V_cube : V_sphere = a^3 : (1/6)πa^3

  The volume of a sphere is given by 4/3(πr^3), where r is the radius of the sphere.
  A sphere fits inside a cube of side length s such that the diameter of the sphere is equal to the length of each side of the cube.
  The diameter of such a sphere is s, so its radius is s/2.

Action: 
  The volume of the cube is s^3.
  The volume of the sphere is (4/3)π(s/2)^3 = (π/6)s^3.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to that of the sphere is s^3 : (π/6)s^3 = (6/π) : 1.
  
Answer("D")

Question: There are ten lime soda bottles on a table in a restaurant. They are to be served among two different groups of customers consisting of 5 members each. How many ways are there to create these 2 groups?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 105
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  There are formulas in combinatorics to calculate permutations and combinations. n choose k combinations is computed by the formula (n!)/(k!(n-k)!); where n is the total number of items, and k is the group size. The combination of n choose k also means the number of ways to create groups of k items out of a total of n items. 

Action: 
  Here, we are trying to create two groups of 5 out of a total of 10 lime soda bottles. We can use the combination formula ((10!)/(5!(10-5)!) * ((5!)/(5!(5-5)!)) to calculate the required number of ways to serve the lime soda bottles among the two groups. The first part of the formula calculates the way to pick 5 items from 10 items to form the first group, and the second part of the formula calculates the way to pick 5 items from the remaining 5 items to form the second group. 
  Simplifying the formula, we get (10 x 9 x 8 x 7 x 6)/(5 x 4 x 3 x 2 x 1) * (5 x 4 x 3 x 2 x 1)/(5 x 4 x 3 x 2 x 1) = 252.
  Therefore, the answer is D:  252.

Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let V be the number of infected files that are infected by a virus only.
  Let W be the number of infected files that are infected by a worm only.
  Let B be the number of infected files that are infected by both a virus and a worm.
  We know that V + W + B = 250
  We also know that W = 2.5B
  We also know that V + B = 0.5(250), because 50% of the files are not infected with a virus.
Action: 
  Substituting W = 2.5B into the first equation we get V + (2.5B) + B = 250
  Simplifying the equation gives V + 3.5B = 250.
  Substituting V + B = 0.5(250) into the equation we get (0.5)250 + 2B = 250
  Simplifying this equation gives us B = 62.5.
  Since W = 2.5B, then W = 156.25.
  The number of files NOT infected by a worm is 250 - W = 93.75, which is closest to 100.
  Answer: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Let A be the set of files infected by the virus
  Let B be the set of files infected by the worm
  Let |X| be the number of elements in set X.
  
  We know that |A ∪ B| = 250
  Also, we know |B\A| = 2.5 |A ∩ B| --> equation 1
  We also know that |A^c| = 0.5*250 = 125, where ^c is the complement
  
  Note that |A ∪ B| = |A| + |B| - |A ∩ B| 
  Therefore, |A ∩ B| = |A| + |B| - |A ∪ B| --> equation 2
  
  We want to find |A^c ∩ B|. 
  We know that |A^c ∩ B| = |B| - |A ∩ B|
  
  Therefore, we need to find |B|.
  From equation 1, we have |B\A| = 2.5 |A ∩ B|
  Therefore, |B| = |A ∩ B| + |B\A| = 3.5|A ∩ B|
  
  Substituting |B| = 3.5|A ∩ B| in equation 2, we get
  |A ∩ B| = |A| + 3.5|A ∩ B| - 250
  Therefore, 2.5|A ∩ B| = |A| - 250 --> equation 3

Action: 
  We want to find |A^c ∩ B|.
  We know that |A^c| = 125, and |A| = 250 - |B|
  From equation 3, we have 2.5|A ∩ B| = |A| - 250, which can also be written as 2.5|A ∩ B| = 250 - |B|
  Substituting |A| = 250 - |B| in the above equation, we get 5|A ∩ B| = 250 - 2|A ∩ B|
  Therefore, 7|A ∩ B| = 250
  So, |A ∩ B| = 35.7 (approx)
  And |B| = 3.5|A ∩ B| = 125.01 (approx)
  
  |A^c ∩ B| = |B| - |A ∩ B| = 125.01 - 35.7 = 89.31
  Therefore, approximately 89 files were NOT infected by a worm.
  
  Since none of the answer choices is close to 89, the most likely answer is B: 70.

  V + 2.5 * VW + VW = 250

         = 0.5 * ((3500 - 1250 + 5V) / 7)

         = (1250 + 625 - 2.5 * VW) / 14
         = (1875 - 2.5 * VW) / 14

  VW = (250 - V) / 3.5
     = (250 - 0.5 * (250 - VW)) / 3.5
     = (250 + 0.5 * VW) / 3.5
     = 71.43

Answer = (1875 - 2.5 * VW) / 14
       = (1875 - 2.5 * 71.43) / 14
       = 75

Topic: Math
Question: A trader sold an article at a profit of 20% for Rs.360. What is the cost price of the article?
Choices:
  A: 270
  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Profit percent = ((Selling Price - Cost Price)/Cost Price) x 100%
  We know Selling Price = Rs. 360 and Profit Percent = 20%
Action: 
  Let's assume Cost Price as 'x'
  From the given data, we can write the formula as: 
  20 = ((360 - x)/x) x 100
  Solving the above equation for x:
  20/100 = (360 - x)/x
  1/5  = (360 - x)/x
  x = 360/1.2
  x = 300
  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs. 300.
Answer: Answer("B")

  20% profit means the selling price is 120% of the cost price.
  We know the selling price is Rs. 360.

  Selling price = 120% of cost price = 1.2x
  1.2x = 360
  x = 300

  Profit = Selling price - Cost price
  Profit percent = (profit / cost price) x 100
  We can find the cost price of the article using these formulas

  Profit percent = 20%
  Selling price = Rs.360
  
Calculation:
  Let CP be the cost price of the article
  Profit = Selling price - Cost price
  20% of CP = 360 - CP
  20CP/100 = 360 - CP
  20CP = 36000 - 100CP
  120CP = 36000
  CP = 36000/120 = 300

  Let's assume that the Cost Price of the article is "x"

Calculations:
  Profit Percentage = 20%
  Profit = (20/100) * Cost Price = (20/100) * x = 0.2x

  Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit
  Rs.360 = x + 0.2x
  Rs.360 = 1.2x
  x = Rs.360 / 1.2
  x = Rs.300

Topic: Math
Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Let's solve the problem step by step:
Let's suppose that the hotel buys X number of papers on each day of the week from Monday to Saturday.
- The cost of each paper from Monday to Saturday is $1, hence the cost to the hotel for buying papers on Mon-Sat = X * 6
- The cost of each paper on Sunday is $4. But the hotel buys twice as many on Sunday. Thus the cost to the hotel for buying papers on Sunday = 2 * 4 * X = 8X
- The total cost to the hotel = $210.
- Putting all the above information into an equation: 6X + 8X = 210
- Solving for X, we get X = 15

Now we know that the hotel buys 15 papers every day of the week except Sunday.
On Sunday, the hotel buys twice as many papers, which is 2*15=30
Therefore, the total number of newspapers that the hotel buys on Monday is equal to the number of newspapers bought on any one of the other days of the week.
Hence, the answer is 15 newspapers (Option A)

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let x be the number of newspapers bought on any day of the week except Sunday.
  Then the hotel buys 2x newspapers on Sunday.
  The total cost per week for newspapers is $210.
  The cost for Sunday newspapers is 2x*$4= $8x  while the cost for newspapers on the other days of the week (Monday-Saturday) is 6*x*$1 = $6x.
  The sum of the two costs gives the total cost per week = $8x+$6x = $14x.
  Thus, $14x = $210, which implies that x = 15.
  Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday.

  4s + 1(6m) = 210
  4(2m) + 6m = 210
  14m = 210

                  - $9x * n = $210
                  - x * n = 23.33 (rounded to the nearest hundredth)
- Since the number of papers has to be a whole number, the hotel must buy 23 papers on Monday (rounded down from 23.33).

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  If the distance between X and Y is d, and the time to meet for the second time is t, then the total distance traveled by Allen and Bob is d + d = 2d. 

  Let's call the time for Allen to reach Y as t1 and time to reach back to X as t2, then
  t1 = d/54 and t2 = d/54   
  Allen takes t1 + t2 = 2d/54
  
  Similarly, let's call the time for Bob to reach X as t3 and time to reach back to Y as t4, then 
  t3 = (d+48)/78 and t4 = (d+48)/78 
  Bob takes t3 + t4 = 2(d+48)/78
  
  Further, we know that they meet for the second time. So, the sum of their travel time is the same as time taken by the other person to finish the journey.
  
  Therefore,
  2d/54 + 2(d+48)/78 = (2d-48)/54 + 2d/78
  13d = 42*48
  d = 144
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 

Let's assume that Allen starts from point A (represented by X in the question)

Bob starts from point B (represented by Y in the question)
We can use the following formula to find the distance between the two points: 

distance = speed * time

Let's assume that the distance between point A and point B is d, and the time required for both to meet for the first time is t. 

Then from the question: 

distance = speed * time

distance covered by Allen from A to B = 54t

distance covered by Bob from B to A = 78t

total distance covered during first meeting = 54t + 78t = 132t

We know that the total distance between A and B is d. So, the distance remaining to cover for Allen till he meets Bob for the second time = d - 132t

Similarly, the remaining distance for Bob till he meets Allen for the second time = d - 132t

At the second meeting, the distance covered by Bob = distance covered by Allen + 48km

[(d - 132t) * 2] + 48 = (d * 2) 

Solve it for d:

d = 252 km

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Let's call the distance between X and Y "d". 
Let's also call the time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the second time "t". 
Since Allen and Bob are moving towards each other, their relative speed is the sum of their individual speeds, which is 54 + 78 = 132 kmph. 

During the first part of the journey, Allen and Bob cover a total distance of d. Since they both start at the same time, we can use the formula distance = speed x time to find the amount of time it takes for them to meet: 

d = 132t 

They both continue moving, this time in opposite directions, until they meet for the second time. During this time, Bob covers an additional distance of 48km more than Allen. Let's call the distance Allen covers during this time "x". 

Then, we know that Bob covers a total distance of x + 48km during this time. We also know that Allen's total distance during this time is d - x (since he is moving in the opposite direction). 

Using the formula distance = speed x time (with their speeds and the time "t"), we can create the following two equations: 

x + 48 = 78t 

d - x = 54t 

We can solve for "x" by adding the two equations: 

d = 132t 

d = x + 48 + 54t 

Subtracting 54t from both sides: 

d - 54t = x + 48 

Substituting the value of "x + 48" from the first equation: 

d - 54t = 78t 

Simplifying: 

d = 132t 

We now have an equation relating the distance between X and Y (d) to the amount of time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the second time (t). 

However, we still need another equation to solve for "d". We can use the fact that Bob covers a total distance of x + 48km during the second part of the journey: 

x + 48 = 78t 

Substituting the value of "t" from the first equation into the second equation: 

x + 48 = 78(d/132) 

Simplifying: 

x + 48 = 3d/22 

Now we have two equations: 

d = 132t 

x + 48 = 3d/22 

Substituting the first equation into the second equation to eliminate "t": 

x + 48 = 3d/22 

x + 48 = 3(132/22)d 

x + 48 = 54d 

Solving for "x": 

x = 54d - 48 

Substituting this into the first equation: 

d = 132t 

d = 132(x + 48)/78 

Simplifying: 

d = 22x/13 + 48/13 

Now we have two equations for "d": 

d = 54d - 48 

d = 22x/13 + 48/13 

Substituting the first equation into the second equation: 

54d - 48 = 22x/13 + 48/13 

Multiplying both sides by 13: 

702d - 624 = 22x + 48 

Simplifying: 

702d = 22x + 672 

Dividing both sides by 2: 

351d = 11x + 336 

We know that "x + d = 2d", so we can substitute "2d - x" for "d" in the above equation: 

351(2d - x) = 11x + 336 

702d - 351x = 11x + 336 

691x = 702d - 336 

x = (702d - 336)/691 

Substituting this back into "d = 54d - 48", we get: 

d = 84 km 

Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 84km.

Knowledge:
  To solve this problem, we need to use the equation: Distance = Speed x Time.
  When Allen meets Bob for the first time, they have each travelled the same distance.
  After this meeting, Allen and Bob have covered half of the distance between X and Y each.
  We need to find the distance between X and Y.
  A, B, C, D, and E are measurements of distance in kilometers.
  
Solution:
Let d be the distance between X and Y.
Let t be the time they take to meet for the second time.
When they first meet the distance covered by Allen is equal to Bob.
i.e., 54t = 78t - d
Therefore, d = 24t      ----(i)
When they meet for the second time, their time after the first meet is half of the total time taken to meet for the second time.
Let the time taken after their first meet to reach their destination be t1.
Hence, the total time taken to meet for the scond time is 2t1.
Distance covered by Bob = distance covered by Allen + 48
i.e., 78t1 = 54t1 + 48
Therefore, t1 = 2/3hr
Hence, 2t1 = 4/3hr
In 4/3 hr Bob travelled a distance of 78 × 4/3 = 104 km
Speed of Allen's towards X = 54kmph
Hence, he would have travelled a distance of 54 × 4/3 = 72 km
Distance covered by both of them after their first meet = 72 + 104 = 176 km
Distance between X and Y = 2d = 2 × 24t = 48t
Total distance travelled by both of them = distance between X and Y = 176 km
Therefore, 48t = 176
t = 11/3
Distance between X and Y = 48t = 48 × 11/3
Answer: Answer("A") the distance between X and Y is 144 km.
Response 4:

Let T be the time taken for both Allen and Bob to meet for the first time.

54T + 78T = d

Equation 2:

24T2 - 132T = 48

2T2 - 11T - 4 = 0

Equation 3: 
d = 54(T/2) + 78((T2 - T) / 2) 

Substitute equation 1 into equation 3 and simplify it, 
d = 27T + 39(T2 - T) 

Substitute T from equation 2 into equation 3 and simplify it to obtain   

d = 126 km

Topic: Math
Question: A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep?
Choices:
  A: 126km
  B: 144km
  C: 127km
  D: 228km
  E: 128km
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume the speed of the jeep on its forward journey was "x" km/hr.
  If it took 6 hours to travel some distance at "x" km/hr, then its distance can be calculated as distance = speed * time = x * 6 = 6x km.
  In the return journey the jeep increased its speed by 12km/hr, this speed was "x+12" km/hr.
  If it took 4 hours to cover the distance with a speed of "x+12" km/hr, then its distance can be calculated as distance = speed * time = (x+12) * 4 = 4(x+12) km.
  The total distance travelled by the jeep is equal to twice the forward journey distance because the distance covered in coming back is the same as going, therefore, total distance = 2 * 6x = 12x km.

Working:
  Let's solve the equation to find x:
  distance = (x+12) * 4
  6x = 4(x+12)
  6x = 4x + 48
  2x = 48
  x = 24
  Therefore, the total distance travelled by the jeep = 12x = 12 * 24 = 288 km.

Action: Answer("C")

  D = S × 6 = (R - 12) × 6    (substituting R = S + 12)

  S = (R - 12) × 6 ÷ 6 = R - 12

  D = R × 4 = (S + 12) × 4 = (R - 12 + 12) × 4 = R × 4

  3S = 2R

Substituting S = (2/3)R, we get 
  D = 4S + 48 = 4(2/3)R + 48 = (8/3)R + 48 
We don't know the value of R, but we can find the value of D in terms of R.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  If the number of water lilies doubles every 2 days, then the formula for the number of water lilies after t days is N=2^(t/2) where N is the number of lilies and t is the number of days elapsed.
  If initial number of water lilies is 1 and it takes 60 days to cover the entire lake, then solving for t in the formula N=2^(t/2) when N=2^60 gives t=120.
  If initial number of water lilies is 64, then N=64*2^(t/2).
Action: N=64*2^(t/2) = 2^60, solve for t gives t=30.
Answer: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The lake has 1 water lily initially, and it takes 60 days to fully cover the lake.
  - Every 2 days, the number of water lilies doubles. 

Solution:
  If it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies starting with only 1 water lily, this means the number of water lilies doubles 30 times (since 2^30 is approximately 1 billion, which is greater than the number of lilies needed to cover the lake).
  Therefore, if there were 64 water lilies originally, this is equivalent to 2^6 water lilies (since the number doubles every 2 days, and 64 is 2^6). Therefore, we need the number of times the number doubles to reach 2^30 when starting with 2^6.
  This is the same as the number of times the number doubles starting with 1, which is 30 days. Since the number doubles every 2 days, the answer is 30 x 2 = 60 days. 
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then after n doubling-periods, there will be 2^n times more lilies than at the beginning.
  If there is 1 water lily initially and it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered, we can find how many times the number of lilies doubles: 60 / 2 = 30.
  Therefore, in 30 doubling-periods, the number of lilies increases by 2^30. 
  If there are 64 lilies initially, in order to reach 2^30 times as many lilies, we need to double the current amount of lilies (64) 30 times.
  2^30 / 64 = 2^(10-1) / 1 = 512
  So the lake will be fully covered with lilies in 30 * 2 = 60 days when there are initially 64 lilies on the lake. 

Action: Answer("C")

  If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies.
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on it, then at day 0 there are 64 lilies on the lake, at day 2 there will be 128 lilies, at day 4 there will be 256 lilies and so on.
  We need to find out in how many days the number of lilies will reach a number greater than the maximum number of lilies needed to fully cover the lake (after 60 days when initially there was only one lily).
  
Action: Answer("D")  

To find out how many days it will take to reach the maximum number of lilies that fully cover the lake, 
  let M be the maximum number of lilies. M=2^((60 days)/2)=2^30=1073741824
  initially there were 64 lilies on the lake, so we need to find out in how many times 64 will double to reach M.
  M = 64 * 2^n => 1073741824/64 = 2^(n) => 2^16 = 2^n => n = 16. So it will take 16*2 = 32 days to reach the maximum number of lilies.
Since there are no answer choices that match 32 days, we choose the closest option, which is D: 53 days (which is greater than 32 days).
Response 5:
Knowledge:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, we have an exponential growth with base 2.
  If there is exactly one water lily on day zero it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered. 
  We want to determine how many days it will take when there are initially 64 water lilies.
  To solve the problem, we can use the formula: N(t) = N(0) * (2^(t/2)).
Action: 
  Using the formula above, we have:
  N(t) = 64 * (2^(t/2)) = 2^6 * 2^(t/2) = 2^(t/2 + 6)
  We want to know when the lake is fully covered, i.e., when N(t) = C, where C is the capacity of the lake in number of water lilies.
  Since the lake is fully covered with one water lily on day zero, we have C = 1 * (2^(60/2)) = 2^30.
  Therefore, we solve the equation 2^(t/2 + 6) = 2^30 to obtain t = 2*(30 - 6) = 48.

Response 6:
Knowledge:
  - If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the growth can be modeled by an exponential function of the form f(t) = ab^(t/2), where t is the time in days, a is the initial number of water lilies, and b is the growth factor (2 in this case).
  - If it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies starting from one water lily, then we can set up an equation and solve for the growth factor b:
    f(60) = ab^(60/2) = a(b^30) = 2^k, where k is the number of water lilies on the lake after 60 days.
    Since we know that k equals the maximum number of water lilies the lake can have, we have k = log2(2^k) = 2^30
    Therefore, 2^30 = a(b^30) => b = 2^(1/30)
    Thus, the function representing the number of water lilies on the lake is f(t) = 2^(t/60)
Action:

  Therefore, t/60 = 6 => t = 360/2 = 180

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 83 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Train M takes 4 hours to go from A to B.
  - Train N takes 3.5 hours to go from B to A.
  - The distance between A and B is the same for both trains.
  - If we represent by "t" the time elapsed since 5 am when both trains meet, then:
    - Train M has traveled for "t" hours
    - Train N has traveled for "t-2" hours, because it left 2 hours later.
Action: Answer("B")  
  - Using "d = rt" (distance equals rate times time), we know that the distance traveled by each train should be the same when they meet. Therefore:
    - Distance traveled by Train M = rM * t (where rM = rate of Train M)
    - Distance traveled by Train N = rN * (t-2) (where rN = rate of Train N)
    - Distance traveled by both trains = distance between A and B
    - We can equate the two equations above and solve for t:
      - rM * t = rN * (t-2)
      - rMt = rNt - 2rN
      - t(rM-rN) = 2rN
      - t = 2rN / (rM - rN) (for t > 2)
    - The time elapsed since 5 am when both trains meet is t = 2 * (distance between A and B) / (total time taken by both trains)
    - Total time taken by both trains = 4 + 3.5 = 7.5 hours
    - Let's assume the distance between A and B is 1 unit (it doesn't matter what unit)
    - The speed of Train M is rM = dM / 4 = 0.25 units/hour
    - The speed of Train N is rN = dN / 3.5 = 0.2857 units/hour (approx.)
    - Therefore, t = 2 * 1 / 0.0357 = 55.6 hours (approx.)
    - The trains meet at 5:55 + 0.6 hours = 6:15 am (approx.).
    - None of the answer choices is exactly 6:15 am, but answer B ("1 hr 15 min") is the closest.
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Train M travels from City A to City B and it takes 4 hours.
  Train N travels from City B to City A and it takes 3.5 hours.
  Total time elapsed from when Train M leaves City A to when Train N reaches City A is  4 + 3.5 = 7.5 hours.
  The time when the two trains cross each other is going to be between 7am and 9am, and it is going to be closer to 9am than 7am.
  A, B, C, D, and E provide specific time intervals for the two trains crossing each other.
Action: Answer("B") which is 1 hr 15 min. 
  The two trains cross each other exactly 1 hr 15 min after Train N leaves City B, which is 8:15am.

Then, you would have to use the time when each train departs to calculate when they cross each other. However, noticing that the answer is closer to 1 hr 15 min than 1 hr 23 min, 1 hr 8 min, 56 min, or 55 min, can be a useful shortcut.

  3. When Train M and Train N meet, they would have collectively traveled the same distance between City A and City B.
  4. Let's assume they meet X hours after Train N has departed City B.
  5. Speed of Train M = Distance/Time, Speed of Train N = Distance/Time.

  7. We can use the above two equations to get the time required to meet.

Response 4:
Knowledge:
  The distance traveled by train M in 4 hours can also be traveled by train N in 3.5 hours.
  Therefore, if the two trains start at opposite ends, they would meet in 3.5 hours.
  To solve the problem, we first need to find out how much time has elapsed since the departure of train M and train N when the two trains cross each other, and then add that time to 7am to find out at what time the two trains cross each other.
  Train M travels for 4 hours (5 am to 9 am), while Train N travels for 3.5 hours (7 am to 10:30 am).

Calculation:
  Let X be the additional time beyond 3.5 hours when the trains cross each other.
  Train M travels at a rate of X+4 hours.
  Train N travels at a rate of X+3.5 hours.
  The total distance the two trains travel is the same, therefore:
  (Rate of Train M) * (Time of Train M) = (Rate of Train N) * (Time of Train N)
  (X + 4) * Train M's rate = (X + 3.5) * Train N's rate
  We know that Train M's rate is greater than Train N's rate because Train M has been traveling longer and is farther away from its origin, so we can use that assumption to make the equation simpler:
  (X + 4) * Train M's rate > (X + 3.5) * Train M's rate
  X > 7
  Therefore, the two trains cross each other 7 hours after Train N leaves (at 7am), which is at 2pm.
  Subtracting 7 hours from 2pm, we get the crossing time as 7am + 7 hours which is 2pm.

Response 5:
Knowledge:
  Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9 am, meaning it takes 4 hours.
  Train N leaves City B at 7 am and reaches City A at 10:30 am, meaning it takes 3 hours and 30 min.
  The time period during which Train N traveled can also be considered as a delay for Train M.
Action: Answer("E")  
To find the crossing time, we need to calculate the total delay of Train M which is 2 hours and 30 minutes (from 9 am when Train M arrives in City B until 7 am when Train N leaves City B). Since both trains are moving towards each other, we can add the travel time of both trains to get the total time it takes for them to cross. 
The total time it takes for them to cross is 4 hrs + 3 hrs 30 min = 7 hrs 30 min. 
We subtract the travel time of Train M from the total crossing time to get the actual crossing time relative to Train M, which is 7 hrs 30 min − 4 hrs = 3 hrs 30 min = 210 min. 
The crossing time relative to 5 am (when Train M leaves City A) is 5 am + 210 min = 8:30 am. 
Therefore, the two trains will cross each other at 8:30 am which is 2 hours and 30 minutes after Train M arrives in City B and 30 minutes before Train N arrives in City A. 
In minutes, 8:30 am - 7 am = 1 hr 30 min = 90 min = 55+35 min => Answer("E")
Response 6:
Knowledge:
  Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am, so its journey time = 4 hours.
  Train N leaves City B at 7 am and reaches City A at 10:30 am, so its journey time = 3 hours 30 min = 3.5 hours.

Approach:
  We know that both the trains meet at some point in between their starting and ending points, and let's say that point is X.
  So, train M travels for 4 hours and train N travels for 3.5 hours before they meet.
  Now, we need to find out at what time they will meet.
  We observe that train N started 2 hours after train M. So, by the time train N started, train M had already covered some distance towards City B.
  We need to find out how much distance they both travel before they meet. Once we know that, we can find the time they will take to travel that distance together using their combined speed.

Method:
  Let's say they meet after traveling x miles from their respective starting points.
  Distance traveled by train M by the time train N starts = x miles (since they meet at x miles)
  Relative speed = speed of train M + speed of train N
  speed of train M = distance / time = x / 4 hours
  speed of train N = distance / time = x / 3.5 hours
  relative speed = x/4 + x/3.5 = (8.5x)/35 miles per hour
  time taken to cover x miles at relative speed = distance / relative speed
  time taken = x / ((8.5/35) hours) = (35x) / 8.5 hours

Knowledge:
  We are asked to find the time at which the two trains cross each other. So, we need to add this time to the start time of train M (5 am) to get the final answer.

Calculation:
  (35x) / 8.5 + 5 hours = (7x/2) + 5 hours
  We need to solve for x, which is the distance they both traveled from their respective starting points before they met.

  x = (time taken by train M to reach X) * (speed of train M)
    = (4 - time taken by train N to reach X) * (speed of train N)

  Substituting the value of speed of train M and train N, we get
  x = (4 - (35x) / 8.5) * (x / 3.5)
  x = 68.75 km

  Now that we have x, we can calculate the time taken to travel this distance together
  (35 * x) / 8.5 = 140 / 17 hours

  Finally, we add this to train M's start time to get the time they both cross each other.
  (5 am) + (140/17 hours) = 8:14 am

Action: Answer("C")

  Train M travels the distance D in 4 hours (from 5 am to 9 am), so M's speed R = D/4.
  Train N travels the same distance D in 3.5 hours (from 7 am to 10:30 am), so N's speed R = D/3.5.

  Let the time when the two trains meet be X. 

  Distance covered by Train M in X hour = R*X
  Distance left to cover by Train N in X hour = D - R * (X-2)

  Since Distances covered by both trains will be equal:
  R*X = D - R * (X-2)

  On solving this equation, we get X = 75 minutes, which is equal to 1 hour and 15 minutes. 
  Therefore, the 2 trains will cross each other at 8:15 AM.

Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?

  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8

  Let the weight of the heavy duty truck be x.
  We have (10 x 12.2 + x) / (10 + 1) = 12.2 + 2.6.
  Solving for x, we get x = 41.6.

Topic: Math
Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The total amount of sand and clay in the mixture is 10 kg. 
  The mixture is currently made of 30% sand and 70% clay. 
  We want to obtain a mixture of equal quantities of clay and sand. 
  To do this, we need to replace some of the mixture with pure sand. 
  Let x kg be the amount of the mixture to be removed and replaced with pure sand. 

We can solve this using proportions and equations:
  - The amount of sand in the mixture before replacing is 0.3*10 = 3 kg. 
  - The amount of clay in the mixture before replacing is 0.7*10 = 7 kg. 
  - After replacing, the total amount of the mixture is still 10 kg. 
  - Let y be the amount of sand in the new mixture. 
  - The amount of clay in the new mixture is also y. 
  - So we have the equation: y + y = 10 - x (the sum of sand and clay is 10 - x because we removed x kg of the original mixture).
  - Simplifying the equation: 2y = 10 - x 
  - We also know that the new mixture will contain 50% sand: y/(y+y) = 0.5
  - Simplifying the equation: y = 10/3 - x/2
  
We can now solve for x:
  - Substitute y = 10/3 - x/2 into the equation 2y = 10 - x: 
  - 2(10/3 - x/2) = 10 - x 
  - 20/3 - x = 10 - x 
  - x = 20/3 = 6.67 kg 

So, we need to remove and replace about 6.67 kg of the mixture with pure sand. 

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
let’s assume the original weight of the mixture to be x kg, then
Weight of clay = (70/100)x kg
Weight of sand = (30/100)x kg
It is given that the volume of clay and sand mixture is equal. Therefore, the volume of clay is equal to the volume of sand.
Now, let’s say that we remove some mixture from the container, which contains an equal amount of clay and sand, and replace it with sand. This means that the amount of clay in the mixture will decrease while the amount of sand will increase. In such a condition, if we want both the amounts to be equal then we must have equal volumes to start with, which means:
1. Volume of sand taken out = Volume of sand added
2. Volume of clay taken out = Volume of clay added

Now let’s begin solving the problem: 

If we remove 'y' kg mixture from 'x' kg mixture, then weight of sand taken out = (30/100)*y kg
Weight of clay taken out = (70/100)*y kg

After removing y Kg mixture, the weight of sand remaining = (30/100)*(x-y)
The weight of clay remaining = (70/100)*(x-y)

Now we need to replace y Kg mixture with pure sand.
If we add 'y' kg pure sand, then weight of sand in the container = (30/100)*(x-y)  + y
Weight of clay in the container = (70/100)*(x-y)

So, both the weight of sand and clay in the container should become equal, hence we have:

(30/100)*(x-y) + y = (70/100)*(x - y)
Solving for y:
y = (2/7)*x

This implies that 2/7th of the mixture needs to be removed and replaced with pure sand.
Therefore, the answer is:

Response 7:
Knowledge:
To solve this problem, we need to use the concept of weighted averages and mixture problems. In a mixture, the amount of each component is proportional to its percentage in the mixture. If a mixture contains A% of X and (100-A)% of Y, then the weighted average of A and (100-A) is equal to the percentage of any other mixture that contains X and Y in equal quantities. That is:
A*w + (100-A)*z = 50
where w and z are the percentages of X and Y in the new mixture, respectively, and 50 is the weighted average of A and (100-A).
We can also use the fact that the total amount of mixture remains the same before and after the replacement.
Solution:
In the given mixture, we have 30% of sand and 70% of clay. That is, we have 3kg of sand and 7kg of clay in the mixture.
Let x be the amount (in kg) of the mixture to be removed and replaced with pure sand.
Before the replacement, we have 3kg/(10kg) = 0.3 or 30% of sand in the mixture.
After the replacement, we will have 3kg/(10kg-x) = 0.5 or 50% of sand in the mixture.
Using the above equation, we can solve for x as follows:

0.3*(10kg-x) + 1*x = 0.5*10kg
3 - 0.3x + x = 5
0.7x = 2
x = 20/7 kg

Action: Answer("B") which is 20/7.

Knowledge:
- The mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay
- To make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand we need to have a 50/50 ratio of sand and clay
- We will be removing some portion of the mixture and replacing it with pure sand
- We need to determine how much mixture needs to be replaced with pure sand.

Solution:
- Let's consider 10kg of the mixture
- The amount of sand in the mixture is 30% of 10kg, which is 3kg.
- The amount of clay in the mixture is 70% of 10kg, which is 7kg.
- To make the mixture contain equal amounts of sand and clay, we would need to have 5kg of each.
- We need to remove some mixture that contains 7-5=2kg of clay and replace it with pure sand.
- Let's call the amount of the mixture we need to remove "x". We want to remove "x" amount of the mixture which contains 2kg of clay.
- So, the amount of clay in "x" kg of the mixture would be (2/10) * x = (1/5) * x kg.
- After we remove "x" kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand, the amount of clay in the mixture should be 5kg.
- So, the amount of clay in the new mixture would be (7 - (1/5)*x) kg, and the amount of sand would be (3 + x) kg.
- Since we want the mixture to be 50/50 clay and sand, we can set up the following equation:
  2 * (7 - (1/5)*x) = 2 * (3 + x)
- Solving for "x":
  14 - (2/5)*x = 6 + 2x
  14 - 6 = (2/5)*x + 2x
  8 = (12/5)*x
  x = (5/3)*8
  x = 40/3
- Therefore, we need to remove 40/3 kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
- To check the answer, let's make sure that the new mixture contains 5kg of sand and 5kg of clay:
  Amount of sand = 3 + (40/3) = (9 + 40)/3 = 49/3 kg
  Amount of clay = 7 - (1/5) * (40/3) = (35/5) - (8/15) = 11/3 kg
  So, the new mixture contains 49/3 kg of sand and 11/3 kg of clay. This is a 50/50 ratio.

To calculate the number of distinct bike numbers, we need to follow these steps:

Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2 x (Length + Breadth)
  Given perimeter = 340
  We can write 340 = 2 x (Length + Breadth)
  Therefore, Length + Breadth = 170
  Let the length of the plot = L
  Let the breadth of the plot = B
  We know that Length + Breadth = 170
  Therefore, L + B = 170
  Also, Perimeter = 2 x (L + B) = 340
  Calculate the value of L + B. It is 170.
  We need to find the cost of gardening 1-meter boundary around this plot.
  The length of the rectangular plot with boundary will be new_length = L + 2 x 1 = (L + 2)
  The breadth of the rectangular plot with boundary will be new_breadth = B + 2 x 1 = (B + 2)
  The area of the rectangular plot with boundary will be new_length x new_breadth.
  Therefore, the area of boundary = (new_length x new_breadth) - (Length x Breadth)
  Cost of gardening is 10 per square metre.
  Therefore, total cost = 10 x [area of boundary]
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  We need to find the cost of gardening a 1-meter boundary around a rectangular plot. We need to know the dimensions of the plot to calculate its area and perimeter.
  Let the length of the plot be L and the breadth be B, then we have:
  2(L + B) = 340, which simplifies to L + B = 170
  The perimeter of the plot is the sum of its sides, which is 2L + 2B
  The area of the plot with the 1-meter boundary is (L+2)(B+2) - LB = LB + 2L + 2B + 4
  So, the cost of gardening will be the area multiplied by the rate of 10 per square metre.

Calculation:
  From the above knowledge we have L + B = 170, then we can say B = 170 - L
  The area of the plot with the 1-meter boundary is (L+2)(B+2) - LB = LB + 2L + 2B + 4 = 3L + 2B + 4
  Substituting B = 170 - L we get, area = 3L + 2(170 - L) + 4 = L + 344
  The cost of gardening 1 square metre is 10, so the cost for L+344 square meters will be (L+344) x 10 = 10L + 3440.

Action: Answer("C")  
Therefore, the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around a rectangular plot having a perimeter of 340 meters at the rate of 10 per square metre is 3440.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of the lengths of all its sides
  Let's assume "l" is the length of the rectangular plot and "b" is its breadth
  If the perimeter is 340, then: 2(l+b) = 340
  Simplifying the equation: l+b = 170
  The area of the rectangular plot is: A = l * b
  The area of the rectangular plot with a 1-meter boundary will be: (l+2) * (b+2) = l*b +2(b+l)+4
  If the rate is 10 per square meter, the cost will be the area times the rate.
Action: 
The area of the rectangle is lb. Since l + b = 170, we can solve for b: b = 170 - l. So the rectangle's area can also be expressed as l(170 - l) = 170l - l^2. We then add 4 to each side to account for the 1-metre boundary, resulting in (l+2)(168-l+2) = (170-l)(170-l) = l^2 - 340l + 28900. Finally, the cost will be the area times the 10-per-square-meter rate, or 10l^2 - 3400l + 289000.

                    = 344 - 2b - b^2

  Capacity in litres = 120,000 litres

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Let's assume:
  Joe's age = J
  Joe's sister's age = S
  Joe’s fathers age = F

From the first statement:
  J + S + F = 100  ---- Equation (1)

From the second statement, we know when Joe is as old as his father, his sister will be twice as old as now
So, let's assume n is the number of years until Joe is as old as his father, then:
  (J + n) + 2*(S + n) = F + n     ---- Equation (2)

From the third statement, we know when Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father
Let's assume m is the number of years since the time Joe's sister was as old as her father, then:
  F + n = 2*(S - m)        ---- Equation (3)

We need to find F, Joe's father's age. Let's solve the equations above to find the value of F.

First, let's solve equation (3):
  F + n = 2*(S - m)
  F = 2*(S - m) - n     ---- Equation (4)

Then, let's solve equation (2) using equation (4):
  (J + n) + 2*(S + n) = 2*(S - m) - n
  J + 5*n + 2*m = 0     ---- Equation (5)

From equation (1), we know that:
  J + S + F = 100
  J = 100 - S - F

Substituting J with 100 - S - F in equation (5), we get:
  (100 - S - F) + 5*n + 2*m = 0
  n = (S + F - 100)/5  - 2*m/5   ---- Equation (6)

Substituting n from equation (6) into equation (4), we get:
  F = 2*S/5 - 4*m/5 + 2*F/5 - (2*S - 100)/25     ---- Equation (7)

Substituting n from equation (6) into equation (2), we get:
  (100 - S - F)/2 + 3*(S + F - 100)/10 + 2*m = F + (S + F - 100)/5
  7*F - 6*S = 100     ---- Equation (8)

Now we have two equations, equation (7) and equation (8), with two variables (F and S), which we can solve to get the value of Joe's father's age (F).

Multiplying the first equation by 6 and subtracting it from the second equation multiplied by 7, we get:
  7*F - 6*S = 100
  -24*F + 24*S = -400
  17*F = -300
  F = -300/17 < 0, which is an invalid answer.

Therefore, there is no solution for this problem. Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
To solve this problem, we can start by using algebra. Let's use "J" to represent Joe's current age, "S" to represent Joe's sister's current age, and "F" to represent Joe's father's current age. 

From the first statement, we know that J + S + F = 100.

From the second statement, we know that when J = F, S + (F - S) * 2. That simplifies to 3S - 2F = S.

From the third statement, we know that when J = F, F = 2 * (S - (F - S)). That simplifies to 3F - 4S = S. 

Now we have two equations with two unknowns (3S - 2F = S and 3F - 4S = S). We can solve for S and F using any method we want (substitution, elimination, etc.). For simplicity, let's use substitution:

- Rearrange the first equation to get S = 2F - 2J.
- Substitute 2F - 2J for S in the second equation: 3(2F - 2J) - 2F = 2F - 2J.
- Simplify: 6F - 6J - 2F = 2F - 2J.
- Rearrange: 4F = 4J + S.
- Substitute 2F - 2J for S: 4F = 4J + 2F - 2J.
- Simplify: 2F = 2J.
- Therefore: F = J.

Now we know that Joe's current age is equal to his father's current age. We also know that their ages and Joe's sister's age add up to 100. So:

- F + F + S = 100.
- 2F + S = 100.
- Substitute F = J: 3J + S = 100.
- Substitute F = J in one of the earlier equations: 3S - 2J = S.
- Simplify: 2S = 2J.
- Therefore: S = J.

So we now know that Joe's current age is equal to his sister's current age, which means that Joe and his sister together are half of the total current age (which is 100). Therefore, their total current age is 50, and since Joe's age is equal to his father's age, the father's age is also 50.

  - Joe's age be x
  - Joe's sister's age be y
  - Joe's father's age be z

  We are trying to find the age of Joe's father, z. We need to use the other sentences to create equations to solve for z.
  When Joe is as old as his father, we know that x + z = 2*(y + k)       where k is the number of years that has passed until Joe is as old as his father
  When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father, we know that: z = 2*(y - k)
  
  By solving these three equations simultaneous we can find all the values:
  x+y+z = 100 
  x + z - 2y = 2k
  z - 2y = -2k

  x+z = 0, which means x = -z

  -z + y + z = 100 => y = 100 - z
  
  Plugging in x = -z and y = 100 - z in the second equation, we have:
  -z + z - 2(100 - z) = 2k => k = -z+50
  
  Plugging in k = -z+50 and y = 100 - z in the third equation, we have:
  z = 2*(-2(-z+50) + 100 - z) => 5z = 300 => z = 60

  (100 - 2F)/3 + F = 2(F/2)
  100 - 2F + 3F = 4F
  F = 50

Response 8:
Let's solve the problem by using system of equations:
Let x be Joe's age, y be Joe's sister's age, and z be Joe's father's age
From the first statement, we have:
x + y + z = 100  ...(1)
From the second statement, we know that:
x + z = 2(y)  ...(2)
From the third statement, we know that:
z = 2(y - (x-z))   ...(3)
Now, we can solve the equation system.
Expanding Eq(3):
z = 2y - 2x + 2z
Simplifying:
-2x + y + z = 0  ...(4)

Now we have 3 equations:
x + y + z = 100  ...(1)
x + z = 2(y)  ...(2)
-2x + y + z = 0  ...(4)

We can solve these equations by substitution or elimination. Here is the solution using elimination:

From equation (2), we have:
z = 2y - x  ...(5)
Substituting z and x in equation (1) using equations (4) and (5)
y + (2y - x) - 2x + y = 100
Simplifying:
4y - 3x = 100

From equations (4) and (5):
-2x + y + (2y - x) = 0
Simplifying:
y = x/3

Substituting y= x/3 in 4y - 3x = 100:
4(x/3) - 3x = 100
Solving for x:
x = 36

Substituting x in (4):
-2(36) + y + z = 0
Simplifying:
y+z=72

Substituting y= 36/3 = 12 in y+z=72:
12 + z = 72
Solving for z,  we get:
z = 60

Therefore, Joe's father's age is 60.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  1. Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan each time the coin lands on Heads.
  2. Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher each time the coin lands on Tails.
  3. After twenty coin flips, neither of them won or lost any amount.
  4. Let's assume that the coin landed on Heads x times and it landed on Tails y times.
  5. The total number of coin flips is 20 times.
  6. Each coin flip can only result in Heads or Tails.

Solution:
  1. Christopher and Jonathan played for 20 coin flips and no one gained or lost any amount.
  2. Therefore, the total amount Christopher gave should be equal to the total amount Jonathan gave.
  3. Christopher gave $2 x Heads times.
  4. Jonathan gave $3 x Tails times.
  5. For the total amount given to be equal, we can equate them:
     2 x Heads = 3 x Tails
     2H = 3(20-H)
     2H = 60-3H
     5H = 60
     H = 12
  6. Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.

Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
- For every Head, Christopher pays $2 to Jonathan.
- For every Tail, Jonathan pays $3 to Christopher.
- After flipping the coin 20 times, both did not win or lose money.
- The total value of coin flips is therefore $0.
 
Action: Answer("8")

Explanation:
- If the coin landed on Heads x times, then Christopher will pay $2 x times to Jonathan.
- And, if the coin landed on Tails y times, then Jonathan will pay $3 y times to Christopher.
- We know that the total number of flips is 20, so x+y=20.
- Also, the total value of the flips is $0, so:
     2x - 3y = 0
     2x = 3y
     x = (3/2)y
- Since x and y are integers, y must be a multiple of 2 and 3. 
- The only multiple of 2 and 3 in the choice is 6, thus y=6. 
- Therefore, x = 3y/2 = (3*6)/2 = 9.
- So, the coin landed on Heads 9 times. 
- Answer("D")
Response 2:
The number of times the coin turned heads will be equal to the number of times the coin turned tails for both of them to not keep or lose any money. Let's assume that the coin turned heads x times and turned tails 20-x times. By the rules of the bet, Christopher would give Jonathan 2 dollars x times and Jonathan would give Christopher 3 dollars (20-x) times. Since the total amount of money given to each other is the same, we can equate the total amounts given i.e:

2x = 3(20-x)

Solving for x:

2x = 60 - 3x

5x = 60

x = 12

Therefore, the number of times the coin turned heads is 12.

  ------------------

  H + T = 20
  
  H + 10 = 20
  
  H = 10

So the coin landed on Heads 10 times.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To solve the problem, we can use the formula: distance = rate x time.
  Let's say the distance between A and B is d.
  For the first part of the trip, Kevin traveled from A to B at a rate of 70 mph, and for the second part, he traveled from B back to A at a rate of 90 mph.
  Let's call the time it took Kevin to travel from A to B as t. We know that it took him the exact same amount of time to travel from B back to A. We also know that he was 70 miles away from B exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip.

Solution:
  We need to form an equation to solve for the distance d:

  d = rate x time

  For the first part of the trip, Kevin traveled at a rate of 70 mph, and the time he took is t, so:

  d = 70t

  For the second part of the trip, Kevin traveled at a rate of 90 mph, and the time he took is also t, but he was 70 miles away from B exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip. So, the time he had left to complete his trip is t - 3. Therefore:

  d = 90(t - 3) + 70

  Now we can equate these two expressions to solve for d:

  70t = 90(t - 3) + 70
  
  70t = 90t - 270 + 70
  
  0 = 20t - 200
  
  t = 10

  Now that we know t=10, we can substitute it into either of the two equations for d, and get:

  d = 70t = 70 x 10 = 700

  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 700 miles.

Action: Answer("E")

70 = d - 70(90/(90-70)) - 70

Solving for d:
d = 270 miles. 

Therefore, the answer is C: 270.

- The time it takes Kevin to go one way is t1 = x/70
- The time it takes Kevin to go the other way is t2 = x/90

    * The time he has been driving at 90 mph was t2 - 3
    * The time he has been driving at 70 mph was t1 + t2 - 3
    * The distance he has covered driving at 90 mph is 90 * (t2-3)
    * The distance he has covered driving at 70 mph is 70 * (t1+t2-3)
    * The total distance he still had to cover was x - 70

  90(x/90 - 3) + 70(x/70 + x/90 - 3) = x - 70
  x*(19/126) = 70 + 27
  x = 270

  We know that Kevin's total travel time is t1 + t2, and we know that he was 3 hours away from the end of the trip when he was still approaching B, so we can write another equation:
  t1 + t2 - 3 = d/90

  Plug in t1 - t2 = -1/35 to get:
  (t1 + t2) - 3 = d/90 - 1/35
  t1 + t2 = d/90 - 32/35

  Now it's just a matter of solving the system of equations:
  t1 + t2 = d/90 - 32/35
  t1 - t2 = -1/35

  Add the equations to eliminate t2:
  2t1 = d/90 - 32/35 - 1/35 = d/90 - 33/35
  t1 = (d/180) - (33/70)

  Substitute t1 into one of the original equations to solve for d:
  d = 70*t1 = 70((d/180) - (33/70))
  d = 35d/9 - 231

  d = 360

Action: Answer("D")

Agent Answer: E

1) ABCDE * 10 + 1 = 3 * (1 + ABCDE)
2) ABCDE = 24567

RHS = 3 * (1 + ABCDE) = 3 * 24568 = 73704

245671 is NOT three times as large as 73704. Therefore, ABCDE is not equal to 24567.

Hence, none of the given options is the correct answer.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Let x be the number of employees in the organization.
Then the amount collected from each employee is given by 6,00,000/x.
If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra then the new amount collected from each employee would be  6,24,000/x.
As per the question, 6,000,00/x + 60 = 6,24,000/x.
Solving the above equation for x we get x = 400
So, there are 400 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Let's assume that there are x employees in the organization and each contributed y amount. We can form two equations based on given information:
1. xy = 600,000
2. (x * (y + 60)) = 624,000

Expanding 2nd equation:
xy + 60x = 624,000

Substituting value of xy as 600,000:
600,000 + 60x = 624,000
60x = 24,000
x = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in that organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Let's assume there are 'x' employees in the organization. 
Knowledge:
  If each employee contributes an equal amount and the total collection amount is Rs. 6.0 lakh, then the per-person contribution is Rs. 600000/x
  If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then the per-person contribution is Rs. (600000 + 24000)/x or Rs. 624000/x.
  We can form the equation- 600000/x +60 = 624000/x
  On solving the equation, we get x = 400.
Action: Answer("C") 
Response 3:
Given that the organization wants to raise Rs. 6 Lakh by collecting equal contributions from its employees. Let the number of employees be 'x' and the contribution from each employee be 'y.'
So, the total amount collected from all the employees = xy
It is given that if each employee contributes Rs. 60 extra, then the total contribution will be Rs. 6.24 Lakh
i.e., xy + 60x = Rs. 624000
==> x(y+60) = 624000
==> x = 624000 / (y+60)

Now let's find the value of y. 
If the total amount collected is Rs. 6 lakh, then xy = 6,00,000
==> x*y = 600000
Substituting the value of x from the above equation, we get:
[(624000)/(y+60)] * y = 6,00,000
==> y^2 + 60y - 2400 = 0
==> y^2 + 80y -20y - 2400 = 0
==> y(y+80) - 20(y+80) = 0
==> (y+80)(y-20) = 0
==> y = 20 (as y can't be negative)

Now, we can find the value of x using the above formulas.
==> x = 600000/20 = 30000/1 = 30000

Each son receives 5*X

Total amount = 4*(amount given to each nephew) + 5*(amount given to each son) + 4*(amount given to each daughter)

8600 = 4*X*2 + 5*X*5 + 4*X*4

X = 176

So each nephew receives Rs 176.

Now we can use this to find the amount that each daughter receives:

So each daughter receives Rs 704, which is option E.

Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  If we call the unknown number "x", then the correct result is 7/8 * x, while the student calculated 7/18 * x. So the student's calculation is only 1/2 of the correct one.
  The difference between the student's result and the correct result is 770.
Action: 
  The difference between the student's result and the correct result is half of the correct result minus the student's result:
  7/8 * x - 7/18 * x = 2 * (7/18 * x) - 7/18 * x = 7/18 * x
  We know that 7/18 * x = 770, so x = 1540 * 2 = 3080.
  Answer: ("E"). None of the above answers is correct.
Response 1:
Let's assume the number we need to find is x.

Let's calculate the difference between the two values: 

(7/8)*x - (7/18)*x = 770/1

To simplify this, we need to find the least common multiple of 8 and 18, which is 72. 

(7/8)*72x - (7/18)*72x = 77*72
63x - 28x = 5544
35x = 5544
x = 158.4

As the answer requires the value of 'x', we need to multiply the above result by 10.

  To maximize the distance, we want to minimize the number of additional quarter miles.
  If we call the number of additional quarter miles "x", then the total miles we can travel is (0.25 + 0.25x) miles. 
  We also need to subtract the initial $3.50 from the $8.50 to get the amount we have left to spend on additional quarter miles.

  So, the maximum number of additional quarter miles we can get is $5.00 / $0.10 per quarter-mile = 50 quarter-miles.
  This means the total distance we can travel is (0.25 + 0.25*50) = 13 miles.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
- The cab company charges $\$3.50$ for the first quarter-mile, which is $0.25$ miles. Hence, the total initial cost is $\$3.50$.
- The cab company charges $\$0.10$ for each additional quarter mile.
- We want to know the maximum distance we can travel with $\$8.50$.

Solution:
Let's call the number of quarter miles we travel beyond the initial quarter mile $x$. We know that the total initial cost is $\$3.50$, so we have $8.50 - 3.50 = 5$ dollars left to spend on the additional quarter miles. For each additional quarter mile, we pay $10$ cents, which is $\$0.10$. Therefore, we have the inequality $0.1x \leq 5$, which we can solve for $x$:

\begin{align*}
0.1x &\leq 5 \\
x &\leq \frac{5}{0.1} \\
x &\leq 50
\end{align*}

So we can travel at most $0.25 + 0.25(50) = 0.25(51) = 12.75$ miles.
